                     ❯ LO 7.r   Apply the insider trading regulations.


          INTRODUCTION
                     Under Section 5 of the Securities Act of 1933, it is a felony to use any means of transportation
                     or communication in interstate commerce to offer or sell unregistered securities, unless an
                     exemption applies. Offers can be made through many forms of media, including the mail,
                     phone, email, or advertising.


                                                                                                                        97



S79_LEM_U7.indd 97                                                                                                  24/05/22 11:02 PM
          98         Unit 7   The Registration Process



                                       The SEC has held that even general or preliminary solicitations can violate the Securities Act.
                                       For example, suppose a broker sends a letter to several investors, asking if they are interested
                                       in a proposed stock offering of ABC Company (described in general terms) before an offering
                                       is registered. This would be a violation.


          LESSON 7.1: ASPECTS OF THE REGISTRATION STATEMENT

                                       Filing the Registration Statement

                                       LO 7.a       Identify the types of registration statements.



                                       Form S-1
                                       To register a new issue with the SEC, a first-time issuer generally files a registration statement
                                       using Form S-1. Included in the statement are the following:
                                        A detailed description of the business and its history
                                        Audited financial statements and related financial information on capitalization
                                        Information on the anticipated use of the proceeds
                                        Biographical data on the officers and directors of the issuer
                                        Information on risk factors, including competition, legal proceedings pending against the
                                         issuer, the regulatory environment, and so forth
                                        Information on the issuer’s dividend policy
                                        The proposed price (or range) of the issue and the anticipated underwriting spread
                                       Filing by coordination is available for many U.S. first-time securities issuers. The filing with
                                       the SEC is also filed with the states in which the issue is to be sold. Once effective with the
                                       SEC, it is effective with those states.


                                       Form S-3
                                       Form S-3 is a short-form registration statement available to domestic issuers who are either
                                       classified as seasoned issuers or well-known seasoned issuers (WKSIs). For an issuer to
                                       qualify as a WKSI, they must satisfy the three requirements of SEC Rule 405:
                                        The issuer must meet the requirements of Form S-3. This essentially requires that the
                                         issuer has (a) timely filed periodic reports for 12 calendar months and (b) not defaulted
                                         on any indebtedness or long-term leases.
                                        The issuer has (a) over $700 million in public float and (b) issued more than $1 billion in
                                         principal of non-convertible debt securities in primary offerings.
                                        The issuer is not an ineligible issuer. An issuer can be ineligible by, among other things,
                                         failing to meet their periodic reporting requirements, being a shell company, having filed
                                         for bankruptcy recently, or having been convicted of a felony or misdemeanor.
                                       Qualified foreign issuers may use Form F-3, a similar form to the S-3.

                                                    TAKE NOTE
                                                    If the issuer is a WKSI, Form S-3 has automatic effectiveness.




S79_LEM_U7.indd 98                                                                                                                          24/05/22 11:02 PM
                                                                                   Unit 7   The Registration Process   99


                     Form S-4
                     Form S-4 is the registration statement used for securities to be issued as the result of mergers
                     and acquisitions. Foreign issuers use the similar Form F-4.


                     Form S-8
                     Form S-8 is used when securities are being registered to be offered to employees through
                     benefit or incentive plans.


                     Shelf Registration
                     Through a shelf offering, an issuer who is already a publicly traded company can register
                     new securities without selling the entire issue at once. Once filed, the registration is good for
                     three years and allows the issuer to sell portions of a registered shelf offering without having
                                                                                                                              Unit 7
                     to reregister the security. Because information about the registration may change during the
                     registration period, a supplemental prospectus must be filed before each sale with up-to-date
                     information. Shelf registrations can be used for both equity and debt offerings.


                     Automatic Shelf Registration
                     WKSIs are given the additional privilege of having a shelf offering become effective
                     immediately, without prior review from the SEC. This type of shell registration, known as an
                     automatic shelf registration, is also valid for three years, instead of only two.

                     If the issuer wishes to extend the three-year period the securities are registered, the issuer need
                     only refile the registration statement, including prospectuses. This will automatically update
                     the shelf registration and restart the three-year period where the securities may be sold.


                     Shelf Company
                     A shelf corporation, shelf company, or aged corporation is a company or corporation that
                     has had no activity. It was created and left with no activity—metaphorically put on the “shelf ”
                     to “age.” The company can then be sold to a person or group of persons who wish to start a
                     company without going through all the procedures of creating a new one. Common reasons
                     for buying a shelf corporation include
                      to save the time involved in taking the steps to create a new corporation.
                      to gain the opportunity to bid on contracts. Some jurisdictions require that a company be
                       in business for a certain length of time to have this ability.
                      to show corporate longevity to attract consumers or investors.
                      to gain access to corporate credit.
                     These reasons are open to criticism. Many years ago, it would take months to properly
                     incorporate a business. However, it is now quite easy to do so, at least in Australia, Canada,
                     the United States, and Western Europe. In fact, it can now be done in as little as a couple
                     of hours in some jurisdictions. In Australia, a new company can get registered within 10
                     minutes. A corporation might end up “on the shelf ” precisely because of a bad business
                     history. It is questionable whether a shelf corporation improves access to capital, because
                     creditors and investors look into a company’s history as part of due diligence.




S79_LEM_U7.indd 99                                                                                                     24/05/22 11:02 PM
          100         Unit 7   The Registration Process



                                        Required Financial Statements
                                        Regulation S-X requires companies to make certain financial statement disclosures. These
                                        statements must be prepared in accordance with GAAP. The statements required to be filed
                                        with the registration statement include
                                         audited balance sheets for the last two years,
                                         audited income statement,
                                         audited cash flow statement, and
                                         pro forma financial statements (when a significant business combination has either
                                          occurred or is probable).

                                                     TAKE NOTE
                                                     The term financial statement encompasses all footnotes and related schedules.


                                        Auditor
                                        Along with the financial statements, Regulation S-X requires the statements to be audited by
                                        a qualified, independent, certified public accountant. The auditor is also required to make an
                                        attestation as to the internal controls of the company. The accountant has three choices when
                                        issuing an opinion.
                                         Unqualified. The auditor does not believe there are any material misstatements or errors.
                                         Qualified. The auditor finds exceptions to GAAP and notes any discrepancies.
                                         Adverse. The auditor views the financial statements or internal controls as being
                                          misleading, insufficient, or not prepared in accordance with GAAP.

                                                     TAKE NOTES
                                                     A statement on the qualifications of the auditor must be included with the financial
                                                     statements.


                                        Deficiencies in the Registration Statement
                                        If the SEC believes that there is not sufficient disclosure in the registration statement, the
                                        issuer will receive a deficiency letter from the Commission requiring additional disclosures.
                                        Until disclosure is adequate, registration is not effective. If no information requests are
                                        received from the SEC or those received are satisfactorily resolved, the registration is effective
                                        at the conclusion of the 20-day waiting period.


                                        Cooling Off Period
                                        Once the registration statement is filed, the issuer enters into a 20-day cooling off period,
                                        sometimes called the waiting period. During this period, the SEC reviews the statement for
                                        full and fair disclosure. The waiting period is intended to provide time during which the
                                        investing public and other member firms will have the opportunity to become informed about
                                        the new issue without having to make an immediate decision.




S79_LEM_U7.indd 100                                                                                                                          24/05/22 11:02 PM
                                                                                    Unit 7   The Registration Process   101


                      The Prospectus

                      LO 7.b    Recall the elements of a prospectus.

                      A prospectus, as defined by the Securities Act of 1933, is any “notice, circular, advertisement,
                      letter, or communication, written or by radio or television, which offers any security for sale
                      or confirms the sale of any security.”


                      Communications Not Deemed a Prospectus
                      The definition of a prospectus is intentionally broad. The SEC, however, has ruled that there
                      are a couple exceptions to the definition:
                       Communication sent after the effective date and a prospectus has been delivered at, or
                        before, the communication
                       Notice indicating where a prospectus may be obtained, identifies the security, gives the               Unit 7
                        price (or price range), or identifies the underwriter(s) or selling group member(s)

                                TAKE NOTE
                                Personal conversations are not mentioned in the rule, and are, therefore, not
                                considered a prospectus. Care must be taken, however, to ensure that the
                                conversation is not disseminated to another party (through recording or transcription)
                                or else it would fall under the definition of a prospectus.


                      Types of Prospectuses

                      Free Writing Prospectuses
                      A free writing prospectus is any written communication that is an offer to buy or sell securities
                      related to a registered offering. It can be considered a supplement to the prospectus and may
                      be used by WKSIs, seasoned issuers and unseasoned issuers. Ineligible issuers, however, may
                      not use a free writing prospectus.

                                EXAMPLE
                                Free writing prospectuses may take the form of many types of communications such
                                as press releases, websites, or term sheets.
                      When a seasoned or unseasoned issuer distributes a free writing prospectus, it must be
                      preceded by a copy of the prospectus. This requirement implies that the registration statement
                      must first be filed with the SEC, before any free writing prospectuses may be used. WKSIs,
                      however, do not have the same restriction. WKSIs may issue a free writing prospectus
                      regardless of whether the registration statement has been filed or not.

                                TAKE NOTE
                                A free writing prospectus can contain information beyond what is found in the
                                registration statement, but it cannot conflict with the registration statement.




S79_LEM_U7.indd 101                                                                                                     24/05/22 11:02 PM
          102         Unit 7   The Registration Process



                                                     TEST TOPIC ALERT
                                                     The SEC defines written communication as any communication that is presented in
                                                     writing, print, a radio or television broadcast, or a graphic communication (described
                                                     as follows).


                                        Graphic Communication
                                        The SEC defines electronic communications as graphic communications. These include
                                        audio and video recordings, facsimiles, email, internet websites, computer networks, CD-
                                        ROMs, and mass voicemail messages. Graphic communications are considered written
                                        communications under SEC rules.

                                        An exception to the definition of a graphic communication, however, is for live, real-time,
                                        transmissions to a live audience. This is still considered a live, oral presentation.

                                                     EXAMPLE
                                                     If an issuer of an attractive issue making a presentation to potential investors cannot
                                                     accommodate all the investors in one location, the issuer may have the presentation
                                                     transmitted live to remote overflow rooms without it being considered a graphic
                                                     communication. If the presentation, however, was recorded and shown to a group of
                                                     investors, the presentation would then constitute a graphic communication.


                                        Road Shows
                                        Road shows are presentations made by the senior executives of a company to potential
                                        investors. These shows now frequently take place online. The company must file its public
                                        registration statement at least 21 days before a roadshow is allowed to take place.

                                        During a road show, executives cannot make offers to sell the securities, take orders, or
                                        distribute sales literature or advertising material. They can take indications of interest,
                                        distribute preliminary prospectuses, and publish tombstone advertisements to provide
                                        information about the potential availability of the securities.

                                        Electronic road shows are road shows that are transmitted to remote locations to engage a
                                        larger audience. Both live and recorded versions are allowable; however, if a road show is
                                        recorded and rebroadcast, it would fall under the definition of a graphic communication and
                                        is considered a free writing prospectus. A real-time broadcast to a live audience, however, is
                                        not viewed as a graphic communication or prospectus by the SEC.

                                                     TAKE NOTE
                                                     While an oral presentation itself is not a written communication, all handouts given in
                                                     conjunction with the presentation are written communications.
                                        While road shows may be considered free writing prospectuses, they are only required to make
                                        the same filings as other free writing prospectuses during an IPO of common or convertible
                                        equity securities by voluntary filers or nonreporting issuers. An exception to this filing
                                        requirement, however, is if the issuer employs a bona fide electronic road show. An electronic
                                        road show is considered bona fide if it satisfies all of the following criteria.
                                         It covers the same material as any other version of the road show.
                                         It is available to any potential investor without restriction.
                                         If new material is added to any other road show, the electronic road show must be
                                          updated no later than any other show.



S79_LEM_U7.indd 102                                                                                                                            24/05/22 11:02 PM
                                                                                                          Unit 7   The Registration Process   103


                                                      TAKE NOTE
                                                      Bona fide electronic road shows must be available to anyone. For example, if it is
                                                      posted online, it cannot be hidden within a password-protected page; it must be
                                                      available to anyone who wishes to view it.


                                           Preliminary Prospectus
                                           After filing, offers, but not sales, can be made to the investing public by means of a
                                           preliminary prospectus. A preliminary prospectus, also called a red herring, can be used to
                                           take nonbinding indications of interest. A red herring can be quickly prepared because it is
                                           part of the registration statement. SEC rules permit the omission of information regarding
                                           the anticipated offering price and the underwriting spread in a red herring. This document,
                                           however, must contain the caption Subject to Completion.

            Figure 7.1: The Three Phases of an Underwriting
                                                                                                                                                     Unit 7
            Issuer files registration                                               Effective date—offering
            statement with the SEC                 Cooling-off period               period may begin




              Prior to the filing of the       No one can solicit sales     Sales can now be solicited,
              registration statement,          during the cooling-off       but the firm must use a
              no sales can be solicited        period, but indications of   final prospectus.
              and no prospectus can            interest can be solicited
              circulate.                       with a red herring.


                                                      TAKE NOTE
                                                      In taking indications of interest, it may be tempting for a registered representative
                                                      to highlight parts of a red herring to focus the customer on what the representative
                                                      believes to be the key issues. Marking or highlighting a prospectus is a violation of
                                                      federal securities law and can lead to termination of employment and other severe
                                                      penalties.
                                           If a member receives a check from a customer during the cooling off period that is earmarked
                                           for the purchase of shares of the new issue, the member must return the check. Placing the
                                           check in the customer’s account could be viewed as a sale—not an offer—which is prohibited
                                           until the offering is effective.


                                           Due Diligence
                                           During the cooling off period, underwriters must conduct a formal due diligence meeting
                                           for the benefit of investors who want information about the issue, the issuer’s financial
                                           background, and the intended use of the proceeds. For issues that are expected to attract
                                           national interest, meetings might be scheduled at different locations around the country.
                                           Representatives of the issuer and the managing underwriter attend these meetings and answer
                                           questions from brokers, securities analysts, and the public.


                                           Material Omissions or Misleading Information
                                           If it appears to the SEC that the registration statement contains material omissions or
                                           misleading information, the SEC will issue a stop order, suspending the registration process




S79_LEM_U7.indd 103                                                                                                                           24/05/22 11:02 PM
          104         Unit 7   The Registration Process



                                        because the statement needs a rewrite. When an amended statement is filed, the 20-day
                                        waiting period begins again.


                                        Final Prospectus
                                        Just before the effective date, a determination as to final pricing is made, and a final
                                        prospectus is prepared. At that time, a formal underwriting agreement is signed by the issuer
                                        and the syndicate manager. Once the issue is effective, sales can be confirmed.

                                        Once an issue is effective (cleared by the SEC), the issuer appears to have met all the filing and
                                        disclosure requirements. The SEC never expresses an opinion on the securities being offered.
                                        In fact, SEC Rule 425 requires that the following SEC disclaimer be printed on the front
                                        cover of every prospectus:

                                              Neither the SEC nor any state securities commission has determined whether this
                                              prospectus is truthful or complete. Nor have they made, nor will they make, any
                                              determination as to whether anyone should buy these securities. Any representation
                                              to the contrary is a criminal offense.

                                                     TAKE NOTE
                                                     All buyers of the new issue must receive a copy of the final prospectus at or before
                                                     confirmation of sale. This can be satisfied by the access equals delivery rule discussed
                                                     later in this unit. If sent in print form, the final prospectus must be sent under separate
                                                     cover.


                                        Forward-Looking Statements
                                        Any statements that are not based on historical fact are forward-looking statements. A
                                        forward-looking statement predicts, projects, or uses future events as expectations or
                                        possibilities. Although such statements are based on management’s estimates and expectations
                                        and available competitive, financial, and economic data, they are inherently uncertain. A
                                        variety of factors could cause the results to differ significantly from what is contained in
                                        any forward-looking statements. Put another way, these statements are subject to numerous
                                        assumptions, risks, and uncertainties that change over time.

                                        The SEC, under Section 21E of the Securities Exchange Act of 1934, allows issuers to use
                                        these statements in their annual reports to shareholders, as well as in prospectuses and proxy
                                        material.

                                        To do so, issuers must identify these statements by the use of certain prescribed words such as
                                        estimate, anticipate, predict, expect, and potential.

                                        Regulation S-K establishes guidelines to be used when preparing projections. The basis of
                                        the projections must be reasonable, and the time frame used must be appropriate. The SEC
                                        permits, but does not require, an outside review of the projections made. If an issuer uses an
                                        outside reviewer, it must disclose
                                         the qualifications of the reviewer,
                                         the extent of the review,
                                         the relationship between the reviewer and the issuer, and
                                         all material factors regarding the review process and how the outside review was obtained
                                          or sought.




S79_LEM_U7.indd 104                                                                                                                                24/05/22 11:02 PM
                                                                                    Unit 7   The Registration Process   105


                      Civil Liability
                      All persons who sign the registration statement (e.g., officers and directors of the issuer,
                      accountants, and attorneys representing the issuer) are potentially liable for damages if there
                      is an omission or misstatement of material facts. Suits alleging fraud in connection with
                      any offering of securities must be brought within two years after the discovery of the facts
                      constituting the violation but no later than five years after such violation.

                      Civil penalties apply even when the omission or misstatement is unintentional. If the fraud is
                      willful, criminal penalties, which consist of a $10,000 fine, five years in prison, or both, apply.
                      Civil penalties are generally limited to the loss sustained by the investor.

                                 TEST TOPIC ALERT
                                 All securities issues—exempt or nonexempt, registered or unregistered—are subject to
                                 the antifraud provisions of federal securities laws.

                                                                                                                               Unit 7
                      Prospectus Requirements in the Secondary Market

                      LO 7.c     Recall the delivery requirements for a prospectus in the secondary market.

                      In certain offerings, a final prospectus must be delivered by all members to buyers in the
                      secondary market for a specified period following the effective date. This is termed the
                      prospectus delivery requirement period, and is summarized in the following. This can be satisfied
                      by the access equals delivery rule discussed later in this unit.

                      It may seem a bit confusing to talk about a rule for prospectus delivery in the secondary
                      market, and in the same breath mention an IPO. But, consider that an IPO, once placed in
                      the primary market, will be required to have available the final prospectus for a certain period
                      while it’s trading in the secondary market.

                      The same thought process applies to a company which has gone through the IPO offering
                      and, at a later date, decides to issue additional new shares. The additional issue, once placed,
                      will also begin trading in the secondary market. And for the period described as follows, the
                      issuer must make the prospectus available to the purchaser, which can be satisfied most often
                      by broker-dealers.


                      Prospectus Delivery Requirements for IPOs
                       90 days if the security is to be quoted in the Pink Sheets or over the OTC Bulletin Board
                        (OTCBB)
                       25 days if the security is to be listed


                      Prospectus Delivery Requirements for Additional Issue Offerings
                       If the security is listed or quoted over Nasdaq, a prospectus must be delivered only in
                        connection with purchases at the POP, and once the distribution is complete, there is no
                        obligation to deliver a prospectus in secondary market transactions.
                       If the security is non-Nasdaq, the prospectus delivery requirement period is 40 days.




S79_LEM_U7.indd 105                                                                                                     24/05/22 11:02 PM
          106         Unit 7   The Registration Process



                                                     TAKE NOTE
                                                     If a prospectus delivery requirement period exists in the secondary market, a
                                                     prospectus must be delivered by all dealers—including those that did not participate
                                                     in the distribution.
                                        If there is a prospectus delivery requirement period and the information in the prospectus
                                        becomes misleading due to a material development (e.g., a patent approval, the loss of a
                                        major customer), the issuer has the obligation to update the information. This can be done by
                                        stickering the outside cover page with the updated information. Stickering a prospectus can
                                        be done as soon as the new information is filed with the SEC—it is effective immediately with
                                        the SEC.


                                        Public Communications

                                        LO 7.d       Apply Rule 134 and 135 to public communications.

                                        As a general statement, once a registration statement is filed, the Securities Act of 1933
                                        prohibits the advertisement of the new issue. SEC Rules 134 and 135 set guidelines for
                                        communications, which are permitted during the cooling off period. These are tombstone
                                        advertisements and are extremely limited in scope.


                                        Advertisements
                                        Tombstone advertisements under Rule 134 are prepared by the syndicate manager and are
                                        generally placed in financial media on or before the effective date of the offering. A tombstone
                                        advertisement is limited to information on
                                         the issuer’s name,
                                         the type of security being offered,
                                         the number of shares to be sold,
                                         the POP (or a range), and
                                         the names of the syndicate members.
                                        SEC Rule 135 deals with tombstone advertisements placed by the issuer, not the syndicate
                                        manager. Under this rule, when an issuer files a registration statement with the SEC, it may
                                        place a tombstone advertisement. The advertisement includes all the information in a Rule
                                        134 advertisement with one major exception: an issuer’s advertisement cannot include the
                                        names of the syndicate members.

                                        All tombstone advertisements must contain the following advisory:

                                              This announcement is neither an offer to sell nor a solicitation of an offer for any of these
                                              securities. This offer is made only by prospectus.

                                                     TEST TOPIC ALERT
                                                     A tombstone advertisement is not considered a prospectus.




S79_LEM_U7.indd 106                                                                                                                           24/05/22 11:02 PM
                                                                                     Unit 7   The Registration Process    107


                      Research Reports
                      Publishing a research report on a new issue is also prohibited. This prohibition begins with the
                      filing of the registration statement and extends through the prospectus delivery requirement
                      period or the requirements of FINRA Rule 2241, whichever is longer.

                      SEC Rule 137 allows broker-dealers that are not participating in the underwriting to publish
                      research on the new issue as long as
                       the recommendation is published in the normal course of its business; and
                       the firm received no compensation, directly or indirectly, from any participant in the
                        underwriting, including the issuer, selling shareholders (if any), syndicate members, and
                        selling group members.

                      Rule 138 allows broker-dealers that are participating in the distribution to publish research on
                      securities of the issuer that are nonequivalent to the security being underwritten.

                                                                                                                                 Unit 7
                                 EXAMPLE
                                 If ABCD were issuing new shares of its common stock, the underwriting participants
                                 could publish research on nonconvertible debt or nonconvertible preferred stock
                                 of ABCD. Distribution participants would, however, be prohibited from publishing
                                 research on convertible debt or convertible preferred securities of ABCD, as these are
                                 considered equivalent.
                      For additional issue offerings, these research prohibitions created a conflict between the
                      information needs of the market and the SEC’s sensitivity to any action that would condition
                      the market to be more receptive to a new issue. The Securities Act of 1933 is clear: sales can
                      only be made through a prospectus.

                      To mediate the conflict, the SEC adopted Rule 139, which only applies to additional issue
                      offerings that meet the definition of an actively traded security (discussed later in this unit).

                      SEC Rule 139 allows research to be published by distribution participants on the security
                      being underwritten if the following conditions are met.
                       The recommendation is contained in a publication that is distributed with reasonable
                        regularity in the normal course of business and includes recommendations on other
                        companies in the issuer’s industry or contains a comprehensive list of all securities being
                        recommended by the firm.
                       The recommendation is given no greater space or prominence in the publication than that
                        given to other recommendations.
                       The current recommendation is no more favorable than in the past.

                                 TAKE NOTE
                                 If an additional issue offering meets the requirements of Rule 139, the quiet period
                                 of 10 days under the FINRA Rule 2241 will not apply. A research report on the subject
                                 issuer can be published during the underwriting period and immediately thereafter.




S79_LEM_U7.indd 107                                                                                                       24/05/22 11:02 PM
          108         Unit 7   The Registration Process



                                        SEC Offering Reforms

                                        LO 7.e       Identify the four classes of issuers.

                                        The SEC has adopted flexible rules relating to the offering process. The following rules, which
                                        are not available to penny stock issuers, are summarized.


                                        Issuer Classes
                                        The rules divide issuers into four primary classes, each entitled to varying degrees of flexibility
                                        in offering securities to the public.


                                        Well-Known Seasoned Issuers (WKSIs)
                                        Firms classified as WKSIs have the most stringent requirements but also the most flexibility in
                                        the registration process. To be classified as a WKSI, a firm must either have
                                         at least $700 million on common equity held by nonaffiliates, or
                                         issued at least $1 billion in nonconvertible securities other than common equity within
                                          the preceding three years.

                                        In addition to meeting at least one of the previously listed requirements, a WKSI
                                         must also be eligible to register securities using Form S-3 (Form F-3 for foreign
                                          companies),
                                         cannot be an ineligible issuer,
                                         cannot be an asset-backed issuer, and
                                         cannot be an investment company under the Investment Company Act of 1940.


                                        Seasoned Issuers
                                        To qualify, an issuer must have at least $75 million in public float value.


                                        Unseasoned Issuers
                                        Unseasoned issuers are public companies required to file reports with the SEC that are not
                                        seasoned issuers.


                                        Ineligible Issuers
                                        The most restrictive category for registration is ineligible issuers. Ineligible issuers are
                                        companies that
                                         have failed to meet filing requirements under Section 13 or 15(d) of the Securities
                                          Exchange Act of 1934,
                                         are blank check companies,
                                         are shell companies,
                                         are offering penny stock,
                                         are LPs and are offering their securities by a method other than on a firm commitment
                                          basis,




S79_LEM_U7.indd 108                                                                                                                       24/05/22 11:02 PM
                                                                                      Unit 7   The Registration Process   109


                       have filed for bankruptcy within the last three years,
                       have been convicted of a felony or a securities-related misdemeanor within the last three
                        years, or
                       have been the subject of a refusal or stop order under the Securities Act of 1933.


                      Shelf Registration
                      For WKSIs, a shelf registration statement is effective immediately.


                      Liberalizing Communications
                      SEC offering rules permit communications by all classes of issuers more than 30 days before a
                      registration statement filing as long as they do not reference the upcoming offering.

                                                                                                                                 Unit 7
                      The rules permit a type of written communication called a free writing prospectus. During the
                      period following the filing of a registration statement, all classes of issuers may make written
                      offers in the form of a free writing prospectus. This type of written communication is an
                      offer to sell or a solicitation of an offer to buy securities that are the subject of a registration
                      statement. A free writing prospectus must be accompanied by a statutory prospectus. In
                      addition, a copy of the free writing prospectus must generally be filed with the SEC before
                      first use.


                      Access Equals Delivery
                      Offering rules acknowledge the widespread use of the internet and the use of electronic
                      communications by adopting an access equals delivery model for meeting prospectus delivery
                      obligations. A prospectus will be deemed to precede or accompany a security for sale if the
                      final prospectus has been filed with the SEC. If you want to see a copy of the final prospectus,
                      log on to the SEC’s website.

                      To preserve an investor’s ability to trace securities to a registered offering, the underwriters,
                      not later than two business days after the offering closes, must provide investors with a notice
                      that they bought securities in a registered offering.

                      The access equals delivery rule also applies to the aftermarket prospectus delivery obligations.

                      Preliminary prospectuses must be printed. Mutual funds must provide investors with a paper
                      prospectus.

                                 TAKE NOTE
                                 The SEC has identified a class of ineligible issuers that are largely excluded from taking
                                 advantage of these offering reforms. Ineligible issuers include those that
                                    are not current in their financial reporting under the Act of 1934,
                                    are, or were during the past three years, blank check (special-purpose acquisition
                                     company) or shell companies or penny stock issuers,
                                    are LPs offering and selling their securities other than in a firm commitment
                                     underwriting,
                                    have filed for bankruptcy during the past three years, or
                                    have been the subject of a stop order under the Securities Act of 1933.

                                                     KNOWLEDGE CHECK
                                                     1.   The interval between the filing date of a registration statement and the date on which

                                                          longer than the current good market conditions are expected to last. Which of the

                                                          filing will be looked at during the cooling off period. LO 7.a

                                                          S-1. Form S-3 is a short-form registration statement available to seasoned issuers

                                                          being registered to be offered to employees through benefit or incentive plans.

                                 6. D An ineligible issuer includes those who have filed for bankruptcy within the last
                                      three years, not five. LO 7.e


            LESSON 7.2: GUN JUMPING AND RESTRICTIONS                                                                               Unit 7

                       Gun Jumping

                       LO 7.f    Define prohibited means of conditioning the market.

                       Jumping the gun relates to soliciting orders or conditioning the market for an upcoming
                       offering before the effective date of the offering. Before the aforementioned securities offering
                       reforms, the only acceptable communication before the effective date for an IPO was a red
                       herring. For follow-on offerings, an issuer could take advantage of SEC rules 137–139.

                       As a result of the reforms, there are now two additional safe harbors to protect issuers from
                       a gun jumping violation. For follow-on offerings, SEC Rule 168 allows a reporting issuer to
                       publish regularly released factual business and forward-looking information at any time. For
                       IPOs, SEC Rule 169 allows a nonreporting issuer to publish regularly released factual business
                       information that is meant for general use, that is, outside of the scope of a potential investor.
                       Factual business information includes information about the business or financial affairs of
                       an issuer, information regarding an issuer’s products, and any information included in reports
                       filed with the SEC.

                       Forward-looking information included earnings forecasts, future business plans, and
                       statements about future business performance.

                                 TAKE NOTE
                                 Road shows have been used for years to acquaint the financial community with
                                 information on a prospective public offering. An electronic road show is one
                                 transmitted by electronic means such as over the internet. If transmitted live, it is
                                 considered a form of oral communication. Recorded road shows are considered to be
                                 a written communication.
                                 Except in the case of road shows for an IPO of equity securities, road show
                                 presentations that are recorded do not have to be filed with the SEC. An IPO issuer
                                 could avoid the filing requirement by making at least one version of a bona fide
                                 electronic road show readily available electronically to any potential investor.




S79_LEM_U7.indd 111                                                                                                         24/05/22 11:02 PM
          112         Unit 7   The Registration Process



                                        Restrictions on Sales of Initial Equity Public Offerings

                                        LO 7.g	Translate the ways FINRA Rules 5130 and 5131 protect the public offering
                                                process.



                                        FINRA Rule 5130
                                        The rule is designed to protect the integrity of the public offering process by ensuring that
                                         members make a bona fide public offering of securities at the POP;
                                         members do not withhold securities in a public offering for their own benefit or use such
                                          securities to reward (or threaten) persons who are in a position to direct future business to
                                          the member; and
                                         industry insiders, such as members and their associated persons, do not take advantage
                                          of their insider status to gain access to new issues for their own benefit at the expense of
                                          public customers.
                                        FINRA Rule 5130 only applies to a new issue, which is defined as any IPO of equity
                                        securities. The rule does not apply to additional issue offerings, debt securities, restricted
                                        or exempt securities, convertible securities, preferred stock, investment company securities,
                                        or American depositary receipts (ADRs) that have a pre-existing market outside the United
                                        States. Also excluded are REITs and direct participation programs (DPPs). Essentially, the rule
                                        applies to IPOs of common stock.


                                        Restricted Persons
                                        Rule 5130 prohibits member firms from selling a new issue to any account in which restricted
                                        persons are beneficial owners. Restricted persons are defined as
                                         member firms;
                                         employees of members;
                                         finders and fiduciaries acting on behalf of the managing underwriter, including attorneys,
                                          accountants, and financial consultants;
                                         portfolio managers, including any person who has the authority to buy or sell securities
                                          for a bank, savings and loan association, insurance company, investment adviser or
                                          collective investment partnership, investment corporation, venture capital funds, or any
                                          other vehicle engaged primarily in the purchase or sale of securities; and
                                         any person owning 10% or more of a member firm.
                                        Any immediate family member of these persons is also restricted. Immediate family includes
                                        parents, in-laws, spouses, siblings, children, or any other individual to whom the person
                                        provides material support.

                                                     EXAMPLE
                                                     Aunts, uncles, and grandparents are not considered immediate family. If, however, one
                                                     of these individuals lives in the same household as a restricted person, that individual
                                                     is a restricted person.
                                        There is an exemption granted to employees of a limited business broker-dealer, which is
                                        defined as a firm engaged solely in the purchase and sale of investment company/variable
                                        contract securities, DPPs securities, or both.



S79_LEM_U7.indd 112                                                                                                                             24/05/22 11:02 PM
                                                                                    Unit 7   The Registration Process   113


                                TAKE NOTE
                                This exemption only applies to employees of a limited business firm, not the firm itself.


                      De Minimis Rule
                      If the beneficial interests of restricted persons do not exceed 10% of an account, the account
                      may purchase a new equity issue. Restricted persons will be able to have an interest in an
                      account that purchases new equity issues as long as no more than 10% of the account’s
                      beneficial owners are restricted persons.


                      Spinning
                      Spinning is the practice of allocating highly sought after IPO shares (also known as hot stock)
                      to individuals who are in a position to direct securities business to the firm. This is why

                                                                                                                               Unit 7
                      portfolio managers are categorized as restricted persons. These individuals are in a position to
                      direct business to a firm and may be willing to do so based on the size of their allocation.

                      FINRA Rule 5131 prohibits spinning. Shares may not be allocated to an account held by an
                      executive officer or director who has a beneficial interest in the company and prohibits shares
                      being allocated
                       if the company is currently an investment banking services client of the member or the
                        member has received compensation from the company for investment banking services in
                        the past 12 months;
                       if the person responsible for making the allocation decision knows or has reason to
                        know that the member intends to provide, or expects to be retained by the company for,
                        investment banking services within the next three months; or
                       on the express or implied condition that such executive officer or director, on behalf of
                        the company, will retain the member for the performance of future investment banking
                        services shareholders, provided that the member firm has no involvement, directly or
                        indirectly, in the allocation process.


                      Quid Pro Quo Allocations
                      Members may not offer or threaten to withhold shares of a new issue they allocate as an
                      inducement to compensate them excessively in relation to the services provided by the
                      member.


                      Flipping
                      Flipping refers to the sale of new issue shares, such as a hot stock, purchased within 30 days
                      following the offering date. Rule 5131 prohibits members or associated persons from directly
                      or indirectly attempting to recoup a commission or credit paid or awarded to an associated
                      person for selling shares of a hot stock that are then flipped by a customer, unless the book
                      runner has assessed a penalty bid on the entire syndicate. The rule also requires that members
                      record and maintain information regarding any penalties or disincentives assessed or its
                      associated persons in connection with a penalty bid in addition to their existing requirements
                      to maintain records with respect to penalty bids.




S79_LEM_U7.indd 113                                                                                                     24/05/22 11:02 PM
          114         Unit 7   The Registration Process



                                        Carve-Out Procedures
                                        Under the de minimis provision in the rule, a restricted person (such as a hedge fund
                                        manager) may indirectly participate in new equity issues through a collective investment
                                        account as long as that person’s beneficial interest does not exceed 10% of the fund’s equity.
                                        To deal with this, FINRA allows hedge funds, where restricted persons own more than 10%
                                        of the shares, to buy new equity issues of the fund to segregate the interests of restricted and
                                        nonrestricted persons and direct the profit from a new issue investment so that restricted
                                        persons receive a benefit not to exceed 10% of their actual fund ownership percentage.

                                                     EXAMPLE
                                                     If 30% of a hedge fund’s partners are restricted persons and that fund buys 10,000
                                                     shares of a new equity issue, no more than 1,000 shares may be attributed in the
                                                     aggregate to those restricted partners’ accounts. In contrast, if 7% of a hedge fund’s
                                                     partners are restricted persons, no more than 700 shares may be attributed in the
                                                     aggregate to those restricted partners’ accounts. Hedge fund managers are required to
                                                     represent to the member firms from which they purchase new issues that the account
                                                     is in compliance with the rule. They will have to determine the eligibility status of their
                                                     shareholders on an annual basis, as representations can be more than 12 months old.


                                        Representations
                                        Under Rule 5130, before selling a new equity issue to an account, a member must obtain
                                        a representation from the account owner (or a person authorized to represent the account
                                        holder) that the account is eligible to purchase a new equity issue at the POP. If an interest is
                                        held by a bank, investment adviser, or other conduit, before selling the new issue, a member
                                        must obtain a representation from the conduit that all purchasers are in compliance with the
                                        rule (i.e., they are not restricted). All representations must be obtained within the 12-month
                                        period before the sale of the new issue.

                                        All records relating to whether an account is eligible to purchase new equity issues must be
                                        retained for at least three years following the new issue sale.

                                                     TAKE NOTE
                                                     The initial verification must be in the form of a positive affirmation letter (i.e., the
                                                     customer must respond in writing that he is not a restricted person). The annual
                                                     verification may be in the form of a negative consent letter (i.e., unless otherwise
                                                     informed, we will assume you continue to be eligible to purchase new common stock
                                                     issues).


                                        Joint Back Office (JBO) Broker-Dealers
                                        Certain hedge funds have elected to become registered broker-dealers and FINRA members.
                                        These firms are known as joint back office (JBO) broker-dealers because they share a back
                                        office with another dealer. Rule 5130 considers JBOs hedge funds, not broker-dealers.
                                        Therefore, these firms can purchase new equity issues subject to the de minimis rule and the
                                        carve-out procedures noted previously.




S79_LEM_U7.indd 114                                                                                                                                24/05/22 11:02 PM
                                                                                    Unit 7   The Registration Process   115


                      Standby Purchasers
                      If, based on indications of interest taken during the cooling off period, it appears that
                      the issue is not selling well, the syndicate manager may allow sales to standby purchasers,
                      individuals, or firms that would otherwise be restricted under FINRA Rule 5130 from buying
                      at the POP.

                      Securities purchased pursuant to a standby arrangement are not subject to FINRA Rule 5130,
                      provided
                       the standby arrangement is disclosed in the final prospectus;
                       the standby arrangement is in writing; and
                       the managing underwriter represents, in writing, that it was unable to find any other
                        purchasers for the securities.


                                                                                                                                 Unit 7
                                TAKE NOTE
                                Securities purchased in a standby arrangement are restricted for resale for a period of
                                three months. Syndicate members are likely buyers in a standby arrangement.


                      Issuer-Directed Sales
                      The prohibitions of FINRA Rule 5130 on the purchase of new equity issues do not apply to
                      securities that are specifically directed by the issuer to certain restricted persons. However,
                      issuer-directed sales may not be made to members, to an account in which any employee of a
                      member firm has a beneficial interest, or to an account in which finders or fiduciaries have an
                      interest. Naturally, there is an exception: if this person or a member of her immediate family is
                      an employee of the issuer, then IPO sales can be made to this account.

                      Also, if an issuer is engaged in a nonunderwritten offering, the issuer may direct sales to a
                      member firm. This makes sense because there are no members involved in the underwriting.


                      Tie-In Arrangements
                      A tie-in arrangement is one in which a member firm, in return for letting a customer buy
                      shares of a new issue at the POP, requires the customer to buy a certain number of shares in
                      the secondary market. This type of arrangement is considered fraudulent under the Securities
                      Exchange Act of 1934 and is strictly prohibited.

                      Another type of tie-in arrangement occurs when banks, which are members, attempt to tie
                      commercial loans made to broker-dealers and others to investment banking services provided
                      by the banks. It is a violation of federal banking law and FINRA rules for a bank to extend
                      credit on the condition that the borrower engages in some other business with the bank.

                                EXAMPLE
                                Examples of violations include providing bridge loans in which the loan is to be repaid
                                out of the proceeds of a bond offering managed by the bank and providing federally
                                insured bridge loans to support a merger or acquisition managed by the bank.

          116         Unit 7   The Registration Process
