          162         Unit 8   Mergers and Acquisitions—Sell Side



          LESSON 8.2: MARKETING AND EXECUTING THE TRANSACTION
                                        LO 8.c      Use marketing activities to attract and retain buyers.

                                        Once the transaction has been set up, the primary role of the investment bank changes to
                                        marketing. It is the responsibility of the investment banker to assist in drafting any marketing
                                        materials to attract and retain bidders. In addition, sell-side investment bankers will need
                                        to assist bidders in conducting their due diligence by being a resource for documentation
                                        requests.


                                        Teaser
                                        The first document a seller would distribute to potential buyers is a short (one to two page)
                                        business profile called a teaser. Teasers are intended to give a brief overview of the company
                                        and its operations to entice a potential buyer to do additional research and investigate
                                        the possibility of making a bid. Generally, a teaser will include a corporate overview, brief
                                        financial history, and highlights of attractive business areas.
                                        An investment teaser is a one- or two-slide summary of a potential sale process (sometimes
                                        without mentioning the name of the potential target company), to maintain the company’s
                                        identity as confidential. A teaser should include the unique selling points of the company
                                        while ensuring that the value of the business is understood by a large audience. A wider search
                                        for buyers helps the target company get the best possible deal.

                                        When a company decides to go for a sale process, the first and foremost objective of the
                                        company is to get the maximum sale price. To achieve this, the company hires investment
                                        bankers or M&A advisors. The objective of the bankers is also to get the maximum value, as
                                        their commission is dependent on the valuation of the business.

                                        To achieve maximum valuation, it becomes imperative for the bankers to market the company
                                        well to potential buyers. Hence, the bankers prepare a professional document known as a
                                        teaser, wherein they highlight the company’s business, financials, projected growth, customers,
                                        and so forth, to attract potential buyers. At this point, the company doesn’t want to disclose
                                        its identity and prefers to remain confidential. Hence, the teaser is prepared without disclosing
                                        the company’s name.


                                        Contents of a Teaser
                                         Important sections that should be included in every teaser are as follows:
                                         Industry overview. A brief summation about the industry and the competitive landscape
                                           where the company operates.
                                         Business description. The company’s capabilities, along with the nature and type of
                                           products or services it offers to customers. One should ensure that this information is not
                                           copied directly from the company’s website, because then the reader might then be able to
                                           identify the company from reading the teaser.
                                         Location. It is important for the teaser to mention the location of the company’s
                                           headquarters. This enables potential buyers to think from a synergy perspective or look at
                                           a deal as a way to enter a new market.
                                         Financial summary. This section of the teaser is very important, as many investors are
                                           only interested in investing in companies with a certain financial profile, such as small
                                           companies with revenues from $5 million to $50 million, or large companies with




S79_LEM_5E.indb 162                                                                                                                      9/1/2020 1:55:34 PM
                                                                          Unit 8   Mergers and Acquisitions—Sell Side   163


                          revenues in the range of $100 million–$500 million. The financial summary also provides
                          forecasts of the target company’s EBITDA margins and other financial metrics.
                       Investment rationale. This section describes the unique selling proposition of the company
                         and the reason(s) why investors should consider buying the business. Examples of
                         investment rationale include recurring revenue, enterprise customers, concentrated
                         customer base, latest technology, proprietary platforms, patents, and so forth.
                       Customer overview. Some teasers also highlight a few of the company’s customers,
                         especially if they are major brands in the industry, to build credibility for the company.
                       Transaction structure. This section deals with the nature of the transaction as expected by
                         the seller. It may be a complete sale of the business, a carve-out, venture financing, and so
                         forth.
                       Bankers information. The teaser also mentions whether the sale process is taken up by an
                         exclusive banker or is a joint venture by two or more banks. The contact details of the
                         bankers are also mentioned, so that a potential buyer may easily get in touch with them
                         for any kind of information or clarification they may seek.

                                TAKE NOTE
                                Teasers for public companies need to comply with Regulation FD. No material
                                nonpublic information may be included in the teaser.

                                TAKE NOTE
                                Confidentiality agreements are also called nondisclosure agreements (NDA), and can
                                be signed before the teaser.
                                                                                                                                  Unit 8
                      Confidentiality Agreements
                      If the teaser attracts a potential buyer, before divulging any additional information, the selling
                      company will require the potential buyer to enter into a confidentiality agreement (CA).
                      This agreement, drafted by the seller’s legal counsel, is a binding agreement that additional
                      information will be held as confidential and may not be disseminated to any other party not
                      listed in the CA.

                      In addition to the agreement that no information specified in the CA will be used or
                      disseminated, CAs will generally include
                       a standstill provision,
                       a nonsolicitation agreement, and
                       a return or destruction of materials clause.
                      The standstill provision restricts the potential buyer from trading in the seller’s publicly
                      traded stock and taking advantage of the nonpublic information they will be privy to. The
                      nonsolicitation agreement ensures that the seller is protected against potential buyers luring
                      away their employees. The return or destruction clause is to ensure the confidentiality of all
                      materials presented. Confidential documents used in conjunction with an M&A transaction
                      will have a control number ensuring all documents may be accounted for. The return or
                      destruction clause requires the potential buyer to either destroy the materials or return them
                      to the seller.




S79_LEM_5E.indb 163                                                                                                     9/1/2020 1:55:34 PM
          164         Unit 8   Mergers and Acquisitions—Sell Side



                                        Confidential Information Memorandum
                                        One of the most time-intensive documents prepared by the seller in an M&A transaction
                                        is the confidential information memorandum (CIM). This document, like the teaser, is a
                                        summary of the company. Unlike the teaser, however, it is very extensive, generally over 50
                                        pages long. It is intended to give a potential buyer sufficient information to begin making an
                                        investment decision and formulate a bid. While the information presented in the CIM will
                                        vary between company sectors, CIMs generally include
                                         an executive summary,
                                         a description of the company,
                                         a description of the company’s sector,
                                         financial statements (historical and projected),
                                         details of firm resources,
                                         details of firm’s suppliers, and
                                         details of firm’s customers.

                                                    TAKE NOTE
                                                    Specific information on suppliers and customers may be generalized when presenting
                                                    the information to strategic buyers. Divulging too much information to a competing
                                                    firm may have an adverse effect on the company and its merger or acquisition.


                                        Initial Bidding Procedures Letter
                                        Once sufficient time has elapsed from the delivery of the CIM, the seller will send out the
                                        initial bidding procedures letter. This letter states the deadline for the initial bids and requests,
                                        including:
                                         The bid amount (generally a range)
                                         Currency of the bid (if cash is included)
                                         Funding source of the bid
                                         Timing for settlement of the deal
                                         Other conditions associated with the sale

                                                    TEST TOPIC ALERT
                                                    Know the order in which documents are presented to potential buyers:
                                                       Teaser
                                                       CA
                                                       CIM
                                                       Bidding procedures


                                        Additional Information Provided to Bidders
                                        Although a substantial amount of information is contained in the CIM, additional
                                        information will always be requested from the seller. The potential buyer may want to see
                                        an additional financial statement or may have questions about the business activities of the
                                        seller. Communication is paramount in negotiating a deal between two firms. This follow-
                                        up communication is done through presentations from management and through the
                                        establishment of a data room.




S79_LEM_5E.indb 164                                                                                                                       9/1/2020 1:55:35 PM
                                                                          Unit 8   Mergers and Acquisitions—Sell Side   165


                      Management Presentations (Road Shows) FINRA Rules
                      The investment banker assisting the seller will work with management in preparing a
                      presentation. These presentations allow management to discuss many of the same topics
                      outlined in the CIM in more detail. The key to these meetings for bidders, however, is the
                      opportunity for two-way interaction. They are able to raise their questions to management
                      and receive any feedback. It is also an opportunity for management to make the offering
                      appear more favorable to a bidder.


                      Data Room
                      The majority of the due diligence process in evaluating a company is done in a data room.
                      The data room contains sensitive documents that are available to bidders. Most data rooms are
                      now virtual data rooms (VDRs) and operate on the same concept as a traditional data room,
                      only in electronic format. VDRs are a password-protected website that contains secured,
                      electronic copies of the same information available in a traditional data room.

                      Physical data rooms are generally in the office of the seller or the seller’s legal counsel.
                      Here, the data room is secure, usually only allowing one bidder in at a time, and is closely
                      monitored to ensure that no documents are duplicated or removed without authorization.

                      The data room generally contains a wide range of company information, including
                       customer and supplier lists,
                       details of company financing arrangements,
                       labor and rental agreements, and
                       other detailed information concerning business structure and operations.                                 Unit 8
                      Because much information may only be accessible in the data room, interested buyers have
                      traditionally incurred high expenses in supplying teams of specialists to be available to review
                      additional or new information.


                      The Bidding Process

                      LO 8.d    Define a nonbinding indication of interest.



                      Nonbinding Indications of Interest
                      At the deadline indicated on the initial bidding procedures letter, anyone interested in
                      continuing negotiations in participating in the M&A must submit a nonbinding indication
                      of interest. This will contain all the information required in the bidding procedures letter. As
                      the name suggests, this indication of interest is nonbinding. There is no commitment, outside
                      complying with the nondisclosure agreement (NDA), made by the bidder or the seller. This
                      initial bid will allow the seller to evaluate all the bids and decide who will move on to the next
                      round of bidding.




S79_LEM_5E.indb 165                                                                                                     9/1/2020 1:55:35 PM
          166         Unit 8   Mergers and Acquisitions—Sell Side



                                        Evaluation of Buyers’ Proposals

                                        LO 8.e      Evaluate a buyer’s proposal.

                                        Bids in M&A are rarely as simple as bids in an auction. Not all bids can be compared easily.
                                        The investment banker, therefore, needs to carefully evaluate each bid for both value and
                                        substance. Some of the issues an investment banker needs to analyze when reviewing each bid
                                        include
                                         the buyers’ ability to pay,
                                         the strength of buyers’ currency relative to the seller’s currency,
                                         an assessment of potential synergies deemed obtainable from strategic buyers,
                                         social issues,
                                         any potential regulatory/antitrust issues, and
                                         any accretion or dilution of the seller’s securities resulting from the transaction.
                                        In addition to evaluating the bids presented, the investment banker also needs to be able to
                                        discern the difference between real and false bids. Not all bidders are interested in closing the
                                        deal. They may simply be trying to get a more detailed look at the company.

                                        When the investment bank has received all the bids and analyzed each, a report of the bids
                                        and recommendations is given to the seller for review. From this report, the seller narrows
                                        which bidders will continue to the next round of bidding.

                                        Once bidders have been selected to move on to the next round of bidding, additional
                                        due diligence continues. The data room will continue to be open to bidders, additional
                                        management presentations will be made, and site visits to the seller’s facilities will be
                                        facilitated. It is the role of the investment banker to continue to field buyers’ requests for
                                        additional information and allow them to complete their due diligence in preparation for the
                                        final round of bidding.


                                        Executing the Transaction

                                        LO 8.f      List the steps that lead to executing the transaction.



                                        Final Round Procedure Letter
                                        The final round bidding procedures are very similar to the initial bid procedures. The bidding
                                        procedures letter outlines the items required in the bid package and the date the bid package
                                        is due. Unlike the initial bidding procedures, the final round bid package is legally binding.
                                        Generally, the final bid package requires
                                         the exact dollar amount of the bid, including any securities involved,
                                         evidence of funding for the bid,
                                         timing for settlement of the deal,
                                         approval from the board of directors (if needed), and
                                         any needed regulatory approvals.




S79_LEM_5E.indb 166                                                                                                                     9/1/2020 1:55:35 PM
                                                                           Unit 8   Mergers and Acquisitions—Sell Side   167


                      Evaluation of Final Bids
                      Once final bids have been received by the investment banker, they will undergo a thorough
                      analysis to determine with whom to continue negotiating. This analysis will involve the seller,
                      the investment banker, and the seller’s legal counsel. Each final bid will be evaluated based on
                      the price of the bid, any legal hurdles to overcome, and conditions required by the bidder.

                      As with the evaluation of the indications of interest, these bids may not be perfectly
                      comparable. While a bid may have a higher price, it may come with conditions that are
                      unacceptable to the seller and would be rejected in favor of a smaller price but fewer
                      conditions. Ultimately, it is the seller’s decision with whom to continue negotiating and who
                      is the winning bidder.


                      Fairness Opinion
                      If the bidder’s board of directors requires a fairness opinion in conjunction with the
                      transaction, the investment banker will assist in preparing it and presenting it to the board of
                      directors. Fairness opinions are discussed at length later.

                                KNOWLEDGE CHECK
                                1.   One of the most time-intensive documents prepared by the seller in an M&A
                                     transaction is
                                       A. the loan agreement.
                                       B. the nondisclosure agreement.
                                       C. the confidential information memorandum (CIM).

                                                                                                                                   Unit 8
                                       D. a confidentiality agreement (CA).
                                2.   While the information presented in the CIM will vary between company sectors, CIMs
                                     generally include all the following except
                                      A. an independent summary.
                                      B. a description of the company.
                                      C. financial statements (historical and projected).
                                      D. details of firm’s suppliers.

                                         and bidding procedures
                                      D. Confidentiality agreement, teaser, confidential information memorandum,
                                         and bidding procedures

S79_LEM_5E.indb 168                                                                                                                         9/1/2020 1:55:36 PM
           UNIT


             9
                                           Mergers and Acquisitions—
                                           Buy Side




          LEARNING OBJECTIVES
                      When you have completed this unit, you will be able to accomplish the following.
                      ff LO 9.a   Explore the situation of the buyer.
                      ff LO 9.b   Determine the preliminary bid.
                      ff LO 9.c   Recollect the fairness opinion content.
                      ff LO 9.d   Recall the required disclosures when providing a fairness opinion.
                      ff LO 9.e   Translate the procedures when using a fairness committee.
                      ff LO 9.f   Identify the standard sections of the definitive agreement.


          INTRODUCTION
                      The focus of buyers in an M&A transactions is to ensure they perform sufficient due diligence
                      on the seller that they have a complete understanding of what they would be purchasing.
                      Along with this understanding is the need to determine what the buyer is willing to pay to be
                      a party in the transaction. While the seller spends a significant amount of time marketing the
                      deal and providing information to buyers, buyers only spend their resources performing the
                      due diligence.


          LESSON 9.1: ANALYSIS BEFORE THE BID
                      LO 9.a      Explore the situation of the buyer.



                      Situation of the Buyer
                      Once an investment banker has been engaged by a buyer, it is the duty of the investment
                      banker to gain an understanding of the overall situation of the buyer financially, structurally,
                                                                                                                         169



S79_LEM_5E.indb 169                                                                                                  9/1/2020 1:55:36 PM
          170         Unit 9   Mergers and Acquisitions—Buy Side



                                        and strategically. This will involve completing a thorough due diligence to assess which type of
                                        transaction would make the most sense for the buyer, as well as the cost and structure of any
                                        bid the buyer may place.

                                        Once the investment banker has established the buyer’s overall situation, she should meet
                                        with the buyer and discuss the rationale of considering the transaction. Why a buyer enters
                                        a transaction may greatly affect bidding strategies. For example, a strategic buyer may be
                                        looking to expand into a new market or introduce a new product line and would be willing to
                                        pay a premium for those gains. A financial buyer, however, would only be willing to purchase
                                        from the seller at a discount to turn a quick profit.


                                        Potential Challenges
                                        When entering an auction for another company, a thorough review of all the implications of
                                        the transaction should be considered before making a bid. Following are some of the issues
                                        and questions that need to be addressed with the buyer while conducting the due diligence.
                                         Legal challenges. Are there any legal hurdles to overcome (e.g., antitrust litigation,
                                           registration in new jurisdictions)?
                                         Control relationship. What would the structure of the company be after the transaction?
                                         Tax implications. Will there be a change in the tax structure or potential areas to claim
                                           new tax deductions or write-offs?
                                         Credit implications. Will this affect the buyer’s credit rating, raising the cost of capital
                                           and difficulty in securing new funds?
                                         Market reaction. Will the markets view this as a favorable or detrimental transaction?


                                        Target Analysis and Valuation
                                        The main focus of the due diligence conducted on the seller will include a review of its
                                        financial statements and market positioning. Investment bankers will need to have a complete
                                        understanding of the company’s current financial situation, its potential for future growth,
                                        and its position in the marketplace. To gain this understanding, research of the seller’s
                                        industry must be completed to determine the industry dynamics and norms to compare with
                                        the operations of the seller.

                                        For strategic buyers, the due diligence must also include a review of any potential synergies
                                        that may exist between the two firms. This includes both immediate synergies (e.g., client
                                        base) and those not immediately available but attainable in the future (e.g., consolidation of
                                        plants). Because these synergies do not exist for financial buyers, they may provide incentive
                                        for strategic buyers to raise their bids so as to eliminate competition from financial buyers.


                                        Nonfinancial Due Diligence
                                        Not all due diligence that must be performed will revolve around the seller’s financial
                                        statements. Additional areas that need to be addressed include corporate governance, potential
                                        synergies, and ways to increase profits.


                                        Human Resources
                                        When performing the due diligence on a seller, attention needs to be paid to the way the
                                        company is currently running and is managed. The largest factor is the seller’s labor. A




S79_LEM_5E.indb 170                                                                                                                       9/1/2020 1:55:36 PM
                                                                            Unit 9   Mergers and Acquisitions—Buy Side   171


                      comprehensive, but confidential, investigation should be conducted to review possible changes
                      in labor contracts, benefits, compensation, and other programs that may be changed to either
                      increase productivity or lower labor costs. An investigation into management may also prove
                      useful during a due diligence. It will demonstrate the effectiveness of management to run the
                      company and may indicate areas of improvement. An investigation into management should
                      be thorough and may include background checks.


                      Information Sources
                      The seller can be a deep source of information during the due diligence process. After signing
                      the CA, the buyer will receive the CIM, which is the first source of significant information
                      available from the seller. Access to the data room will also allow the buyer to analyze
                      information that may be confidential and not accessible to the public. Additional information
                      from the seller can include management presentations and site visits. This does not limit the
                      buyer to only using the seller as a resource because information provided by the seller may be
                      skewed in the seller’s favor. Other third-party sources should also be consulted to verify data
                      gathered from the seller as well as uncover additional information the seller may not disclose.
                      This will allow the buyer’s due diligence to be more well-rounded.


                      Assessment of Other Buyers
                      Because there is competition between buyers, it is important to know the interest and
                      capabilities of the other buyers. Knowing the resources and interest level of the competition
                      will allow the buyer to have a better picture of what the final price will be. For example, if
                      another bidder has significant funds available and is very interested in acquiring the seller, a
                      bidding war may ensue, resulting in a much higher price.

                                        B. the buyer’s company structure
                                        C. the strategical fit if the buyer is successful
                                        D. the location of the buyer

                                       A. The accounts receivable

                                                        and considerations, not the seller’s. LO 9.a

                                                        available from the seller. LO 9.a


          LESSON 9.2: THE BIDDING PROCESS AND EXECUTING THE DEAL
                                        LO 9.b      Determine the preliminary bid.

                                        Once the buyer has completed sufficient due diligence to determine interest in pursuing the
                                        transaction, the investment banker assists the buyer in putting together a preliminary bid. The
                                        preliminary bid must include the elements required in the bid procedures letter, which is sent
                                        to the investment banker. This bid is not binding, but it is an indication of the buyer’s level of
                                        interest.

                                        When putting together the preliminary bid, a buyer needs to begin seriously considering the
                                        funding source, should the bid be accepted. While the seller’s investment banker may offer
                                        stapled financing, the buyer’s investment banker must fulfill his fiduciary responsibility to
                                        ensure the buyer has the best and least expensive source of capital available. This may include
                                        borrowing from a bank and/or offering securities.


                                        Executing the Deal

                                        Follow-Up Due Diligence
                                        Prior to the buyer making a final bid, the due diligence should be completed. This is generally
                                        a prerequisite in the final bidding procedures letter. Consequently, the bidder may need to
                                        access the data room and make site visits to ensure a thorough review of the seller has been
                                        completed, and a value analysis is complete.




S79_LEM_5E.indb 172                                                                                                                           9/1/2020 1:55:37 PM
                                                                           Unit 9   Mergers and Acquisitions—Buy Side   173


                       Final Bid
                       After receipt of the final bidding procedures letter, the buyer’s investment banker assists in
                       determining the final bid, including size, type, and any conditions associated with it. The bid
                       must contain all the required items in the bidding procedures letter and be submitted on time
                       for consideration by the seller.


                       Fairness Opinion
                       If a fairness opinion is requested, the buy-side investment banker may be used as a resource
                       to assist in its preparation and presentation to the board of directors. Fairness opinions are
                       covered in greater detail later in the next lesson.


                       Coordinate Financial Terms
                       Once an agreement has been reached between the buyer and the seller, the buy-side
                       investment banker will need to coordinate with others, such as the buyer’s legal counsel and
                       accountant, to make certain that all the proper steps are taken to ensure the closing of the deal
                       proceeds smoothly.


            LESSON 9.3: FAIRNESS OPINION AND THE DEFINITIVE AGREEMENT

                       LO 9.c    Recollect the fairness opinion content.

                       When a seller receives a bid, one of the steps the board of directors takes in assessing the bid
                       is requesting a fairness opinion. The fairness opinion is a document prepared by a third-
                       party (often the investment bank acting as their advisor) to assess the fairness of the bid. This
                       is a very common procedure for public companies. Public companies are under significant
                       scrutiny by the investing public, and having a fairness opinion will permit the board of
                       directors and management to limit their liability in the event of legal action being taken
                       against them by a dissatisfied shareholder.

                                 TAKE NOTE

                                                                                                                                  Unit 9
                                 Fairness opinions do not indicate whether the proposed transaction is the best for the
                                 company—only whether the transaction would, as the name suggests, be fair.


                       Fairness Opinion Content
                       Fairness opinions are detailed documents that include much of the due diligence that an
                       investment banker conducts on a seller. They include
                        financial statements (both past and pro forma),
                        projections of future growth,
                        comparable transactions,
                        analysis of market trends,
                        valuation analysis of transaction, and
                        assumptions used in generating opinion.




S79_LEM_5E.indb 173                                                                                                     9/1/2020 1:55:38 PM
          174         Unit 9   Mergers and Acquisitions—Buy Side



                                        Fairness opinions can be quite lengthy, but they may be very useful for the board of directors
                                        in making its decisions or recommendations before a transaction. It is very common for
                                        fairness opinions to be requested when a transaction involves a public company, and they are
                                        becoming more popular in all M&A and tender offer transactions.


                                        Required Disclosures

                                        LO 9.d      Recall the required disclosures when providing a fairness opinion.

                                        FINRA Rule 5150 requires specific disclosures related to conflicts of interest, which
                                        could arise when a member firm provides a fairness opinion in connection with mergers,
                                        acquisitions, or the purchase of assets. Fairness opinions express a conclusion as to whether
                                        the consideration offered in a transaction is within the range of what would be considered fair.
                                        In a fairness opinion, a member firm is required to disclose
                                         if the firm has acted as a financial advisor to any party to the transaction and, if
                                           applicable, that it will receive compensation that is contingent upon the successful
                                           completion of the transaction;
                                         any material relationships that existed during the past two years with any party involved
                                           in the transaction and whether any compensation was or will be received as a result of the
                                           relationship;
                                         if any information that formed a basis for the opinion was supplied to the firm by the
                                           party requesting the opinion and whether this information was independently verified;
                                         if the fairness opinion was approved or issued by a fairness committee; and
                                         whether or not the fairness opinion expresses a view about the fairness of the amount or
                                           nature of the compensation to any of the company’s officers or directors relative to the
                                           compensation to the public shareholders of the company.

                                        A member firm that issues fairness opinions must have procedures in place regarding the
                                        circumstances in which it will use a fairness committee to approve or issue a fairness opinion.
                                        Procedures must include the process for selecting personnel to be on the committee, the
                                        necessary qualifications for such persons, and the process to promote a balanced review by the
                                        committee. In other words, the committee should include persons who did not serve on the
                                        deal team.


                                        Fairness Committee

                                        LO 9.e      Translate the procedures when using a fairness committee.

                                        When broker-dealers write a fairness opinion, they are required to have a process in place to
                                        determine whether the valuation analysis used in the opinion was appropriate. A frequent
                                        method of determining the appropriateness is by instituting an independent fairness
                                        committee. When a broker-dealer uses a fairness committee, it must have written procedures in
                                        place detailing
                                         the process for selecting the members of the fairness committee,
                                         the necessary qualifications to serve on the fairness committee, and
                                         the process to ensure the fairness committee is balanced in its review, including its
                                           independence from the deal team.




S79_LEM_5E.indb 174                                                                                                                   9/1/2020 1:55:38 PM
                                                                          Unit 9   Mergers and Acquisitions—Buy Side   175


                      Definitive Agreement

                      LO 9.f     Identify the standard sections of the definitive agreement.

                      Once a winning bidder has been selected, the buyer and seller begin negotiating and drafting
                      the definitive agreement. Also referred to as the definitive purchase agreement, definitive merger
                      agreement, or stock purchase agreement, the definitive agreement is the final, binding contract
                      that itemizes all the details of the transaction. The definitive agreement, while unique to each
                      transaction, will generally contain several standard sections detailing the transaction and the
                      rights and obligations of the buyer and seller.


                      Transaction Terms
                      The definitive agreement will begin with all the terms of the sale. This will include identifying
                      the two parties in the transaction, as well as the purchase price of the company (or
                      subdivision).


                      Representations and Warranties
                      In the representations and warranties section, both the buyer and the seller make
                      representations about their companies. These representations often include items such as
                       compliance with tax and regulatory requirements,
                       complete and fair financial statements,
                       the presence of sufficient internal accounting controls,
                       no material adverse changes (MACs),
                       the identification of all material contracts, and
                       details on the source of the buyer’s financing.
                      The representations made in this section are generally much more focused on the seller. These
                      representations help the buyer ensure they are purchasing what was expected and that all
                      material information has been provided. If there is a MAC, then the buyer would use this
                      representation as reason to back out of the transaction.

                      The buyer’s representation is generally limited to the source of funds for financing the                   Unit 9
                      transaction (e.g., that it will be raised through the issuance of new debt securities).


                      Covenants
                      Certain covenants will be required by the seller as part of any transaction. Generally, these
                      covenants are made to ensure the seller does not engage in unusual activities. These covenants
                      can include
                       limits on capital expenditures,
                       limits on new debt issues,
                       limits on new equity issues,
                       restrictions on special dividends, and
                       restrictions on major asset sales.




S79_LEM_5E.indb 175                                                                                                    9/1/2020 1:55:38 PM
          176         Unit 9   Mergers and Acquisitions—Buy Side



                                        In addition to these covenants, made by the seller, which ensure the company is not materially
                                        altered before closing the transaction, there are also covenants that both the buyer and the
                                        seller will be acting in good faith and using their best efforts to complete the transaction.


                                        Additional Agreements
                                        Most definitive agreements will have additional agreements outside of the covenants. These
                                        agreements could define tax liabilities for each party, requirements to obtain proper financing
                                        for the transaction, and commonly, either a no-shop or a go-shop clause. A no-shop clause is an
                                        agreement a buyer would want placed in the definitive agreement to prevent the seller from
                                        pursuing other unsolicited bids for the company. Since there is a fiduciary responsibility of the
                                        selling company’s management to the shareholders, they must always review any unsolicited
                                        bids. The no-shop clause, however, limits their ability to continue seeking other buyers. The
                                        opposite of a no-shop clause is a go-shop clause. A go-shop clause, which explicitly permits
                                        the seller to actively seek other bids, would be placed in a definitive agreement by the seller.
                                        No buyer, however, would be satisfied with an open-ended go-shop clause. As a result, they
                                        will always have a short window of time during which the seller may solicit additional buyers.
                                        Once the window expires, so does the go-shop clause. This window is generally only one to
                                        three months long. Buyers may be inclined to accept this clause in return for a lower purchase
                                        price.


                                        Closing Conditions
                                        The closing conditions section of the definitive agreement identifies all the requirements
                                        needed to be met, by both the buyer and the seller, in order for the transaction to close. These
                                        provisions may include approval from regulatory bodies. For example, if the transaction
                                        would require reporting to the FTC and the Department of Justice (DOJ) under the
                                        Hart-Scott-Rodino Antitrust Improvements Act of 1976 (HSR Act), the transaction must first
                                        be approved by those bodies. Shareholder approval may also be required by either the seller,
                                        the buyer, or both. All representations (defined in the representations and warranties section)
                                        must also be satisfied on the closing date. As long as these and any other defined conditions
                                        are met, the transaction will close.


                                        Indemnification
                                        The final portion of the definitive agreement is the indemnification section. While this section
                                        is used primarily for private sellers, on rare occasion it will be seen for public sellers as well.
                                        It is intended to be used as a tool to shift liability for any misstated or undisclosed material
                                        information back to the seller. If a material misstatement is found, the seller may be required
                                        to pay significant repercussions. This is not intended to create an indefinite, unlimited liability
                                        to the seller. Indemnification clauses will contain time limits for when a claim can be made,
                                        minimum losses before a claim may be made, and a maximum (or cap) on the size of the
                                        claim.

                                                    TEST TOPIC ALERT
                                                    In a negotiated deal, instead of an auction, the seller finds only one buyer and begins
                                                    the process with negotiating the definitive agreement immediately.

           UNIT


     10
                                           SEC Rules Applicable to
                                           Mergers and Acquisitions




          LEARNING OBJECTIVES
                       When you have completed this unit, you will be able to accomplish the following.
                       ff LO 10.a	Recollect the general terms of the Hart-Scott-Rodino Antitrust Act.
                       ff LO 10.b	Interpret SEC Rules 145 and 165.
                       ff LO 10.c	Recall the need for public companies to disclose the details of a proposed business
                                  combination.


          INTRODUCTION
                       As with any securities transactions, the regulatory bodies have an interest in ensuring an open
                       and fair marketplace. Several laws and regulations have been enacted to ensure that foul play
                       in these transactions is minimized.


          LESSON 10.1: HART-SCOTT-RODINO ANTITRUST ACT
                       LO 10.a	Recollect the general terms of the Hart-Scott-Rodino Antitrust Act.

                       The Hart-Scott-Rodino Antitrust Improvements Act of 1976 (HSR Act) is an amendment to
                       various antitrust laws and requires both parties to an intended acquisition or merger to file
                       information on the proposed transaction with the FTC and the DOJ. Upon filing, a 30-day
                       waiting period (15 days for all-cash transactions) ensues during which time the FTC and the
                       DOJ will make a determination as to whether the proposed transaction violates antitrust laws.

                       It is unlawful to close the transaction during the waiting period. Although the waiting period
                       can be as long as 30 days, the FTC may request additional time to review the information
                       presented. On the other hand, the filing parties may request that the waiting period be
                       terminated early if there are no obvious impediments to the deal.
                                                                                                                              179



S79_LEM_U10.indd 179                                                                                                       9/3/2020 9:28:47 AM
          180          Unit 10   SEC Rules Applicable to Mergers and Acquisitions



                                         Reporting to the FTC and DOJ is only required if certain conditions occur. The dollar
                                         amounts will not be tested on the exam. They usually change every year. These conditions can
                                         be determined through the following three tests.
                                          Commerce test. Either party of the merger needs to be engaged in U.S. commerce.
                                          Size of transaction test. This test deals with how large the transaction is. Any merger under
                                           the $101 million threshold need not file. Any transaction greater than $403.9 million
                                           must always file. Transactions valued between $101 million and $403.9 million must
                                           undergo the size of person test to determine whether or not they must file.
                                          The size of person test. This test requires notification if the transaction has one party with
                                           more than $10 million in annual sales (or total assets) and the other party has over
                                           $100 million in annual sales (or total assets).

                                                      TAKE NOTE
                                                      The thresholds given in the text are the original thresholds listed in the HSR Act. These
                                                      amounts are updated regularly. Following is a chart showing the base and current
                                                      thresholds as of printing. For the most up-to-date information, please check the
                                                      Content Update section of your Kaplan Financial Series 79 website dashboard.

                                                                                             Base Thresholds           2022 Thresholds
                                                       Size of Transaction Test (min)            $50 million              $101 million
                                                       Size of Transaction Test (max)           $200 million             $403.9 million
                                                       Size of Person Test (small)               $10 million              $20.2 million
                                                       Size of Person Test (large)              $100 million              $202 million

                                                      TAKE NOTE
                                                      Related to HSR is Regulation M-A, which has been designed to provide guidelines to
                                                      companies involved in tender offers as well as M&A. Among other things, it requires
                                                      that a summary term sheet be provided to investors as part of the disclosure process.
                                                      The summary term sheet must be on the first or second page of the disclosure
                                                      document and must contain the material facts about the proposed transaction in
                                                      bullet format.


                                         Securities Act of 1933

                                         LO 10.b	Interpret SEC Rules 145 and 165.



                                         SEC Rule 145
                                         SEC Rule 145 requires that securities issued as part of a business combination, such as a
                                         merger or acquisition, must be registered and are subject to the same registration requirements
                                         as other issues. Generally, these securities are registered using the short-form registration
                                         statement, Form S-4.

                                         Securities involved in such combinations must be registered if security holders are asked to
                                         vote or give consent for a plan or agreement involving any of these transactions. Registration
                                         is required whether or not securities holders consent, and whether or not they receive new or
                                         different securities. In most cases, the registration is made through F-4 for foreign companies.




S79_LEM_U10.indd 180                                                                                                                              8/30/23 10:24 PM
                                                               Unit 10   SEC Rules Applicable to Mergers and Acquisitions   181


                       An exception is made for securities exchanged by the issuer solely among its existing securities
                       holders, when no commission or other remuneration is paid to brokers, directly or indirectly.

                       The offer to sell securities in a business combination is not always made by the issuer of the
                       securities held by voting shareholders. In a tender offer to exchange one security for another,
                       for example, the offer is made by the bidder or acquirer, and the acquirer is subject to
                       registration and prospectus delivery requirements.

                       However, in a merger or consolidation that involves the proposed exchange of securities, both
                       the acquirer and target company prepare a combined S-4 registration and prospectus, as well
                       as the proxy disclosures.

                                 TAKE NOTE
                                 This rule applies to securities that are issued as payment, shares in a new company
                                 resulting from a merger, or an exchange in class of securities (e.g., Class B shares to
                                 Class A shares).


                       Rule 165
                       SEC Rule 165 allows for an exemption of communications before registration for securities
                       being issued in conjunction with a business combination. Written communications may be
                       distributed before the filing of the registration statement as long it meets the requirements of a
                       prospectus, including a legend urging investors to read the relevant documentation filed with
                       the SEC in conjunction with the offering. Preregistration communications must be filed with
                       the SEC no later than the first day of use, and the communication may not be an offering, but
                       a general announcement of the securities offering.

                                 TEST TOPIC ALERT
                                 Nonpublic communications, such as a memo between a seller and the seller’s
                                 investment banker, are not subject to the filing requirement.


            LESSON 10.2: REGULATION M-A

                       LO 10.c	Recall the need for public companies to disclose the details of a proposed
                                business combination.

                       Regulation M-A (mergers and acquisitions) was written to address the disclosures required
                       during M&A. It requires public companies to disclose to shareholders the details of the
                       proposed business combination. This disclosure is made using the Schedule 14A proxy
                       statement.


                       Schedule 14A
                       When public companies are undergoing business consolidations, the seller is always required
                       to have a shareholder vote on the transaction. If the buyer is making payment through                          Unit 10
                       securities (which will dilute the ownership interest of current shareholders), the buyer’s
                       shareholders will also vote on the transaction.




S79_LEM_5E.indb 181                                                                                                         9/1/2020 1:55:41 PM
          182         Unit 10   SEC Rules Applicable to Mergers and Acquisitions



                                        When soliciting votes, companies are required to issue a proxy statement and file it with the
                                        SEC. Item 14 on Schedule 14A specifies the information that is required to be included on
                                        the proxy statement. This information includes
                                         a summary term sheet;
                                         contact information;
                                         a brief description of the general nature of the business conducted;
                                         terms of the transaction;
                                         whether or not necessary regulatory approvals have been obtained;
                                         reports, opinions, and appraisals of the transaction (including the fairness opinion);
                                         past contacts, transactions, or negotiations;
                                         selected financial data; and
                                         pro forma selected financial data.

                                                     TAKE NOTE
                                                     The summary term sheet must be on the first or second page of the disclosure
                                                     document and must contain the material facts about the proposed transaction in
                                                     bullet format.

                      5.   As a domestic corporation, XYZ offers to acquire a single class of its publicly
                           registered and traded short-term debt securities for “cash only.” That transaction will
                           require a shareholder vote. For this to occur, which of the following filings must the
                           company make?
                             A. An S-4 registration of the offer only
                            B. A proxy filing, S-4 registration, and prospectus
                             C. A proxy filing only
                            D. None of these
                      6.   When a shareholder vote or consent is required to approve a business combination,
                           proxy information is filed with the SEC on which form or schedule?
                            A. Schedule 13-D
                            B. Form 8-K
                            C. Schedule 14A
                            D. Form S-1
                      7.   The Hart-Scott-Rodino Antitrust Improvements Act of 1976 (HSR Act) requires both
                           parties to an intended acquisition or merger to
                            A. inquire of the FTC 10 days before any announcement of a proposed merger.
                            B. file information on the proposed transaction with the FTC and the DOJ and
                                 wait 30 days.
                            C. file with the FTC and the SEC. Upon filing, a 30-day waiting period ensues.
                            D. wait no more than 15 business days before closing the deal.

                      Answers
                      1. D Both parties to an intended acquisition or merger are required to file information
                           on the proposed transaction with the Federal Trade Commission (FTC) and the
                           Department of Justice (DOJ). LO 10.a

                      2. C Although the waiting period can be as long as 30 days, the FTC may request
                           additional time to review the information presented. LO 10.a

                      3. D There is no requirement for the merger or acquisition to meet a certain level of
                           income. LO 10.a

                      4. A The rule requires registration in any business combination in which securities
                           holders are asked to vote or give consent or agreement to the transaction. LO 10.b

                      5. C Under SEC Rule 145, a business combination offer for all-cash (that does not
                           involve a change of securities) does not require registration or a prospectus. If the
                           cash payment is contingent on shareholder vote, a proxy must be filed. LO 10.b

                      6. C Proxy information is filed on Schedule 14A, the proxy statement, when a business
                           combination is subject to a vote of shareholder approval. If votes or consents are
                           not required, similar information may be required on Form S-4. LO 10.c

                      7. B The HSR Act requires both parties to an intended acquisition or merger to file
                           information on the proposed transaction with the Federal Trade Commission (FTC)
                           and the Department of Justice (DOJ). Upon filing, a 30-day waiting period (15 days
                           for all-cash transactions) ensues. LO 10.a
