          LEARNING OBJECTIVES
                      When you have completed this unit, you will be able to accomplish the following.
                      ff LO 11.a	Identify the precommencement communications and the tender offer statement.
                      ff LO 11.b	Apply the regulations that impact tender offers.
                      ff LO 11.c	Recall the choices issuers have by which tender offer shares may be acquired.
                      ff LO 11.d	Identify the conditions to comply with the SEC Safe Harbor Rule 10b-18.



          INTRODUCTION
                      According to the SEC, a tender offer is a broad solicitation by a company or a third party to
                      purchase a substantial percentage of a company’s Section 12 registered equity shares or units
                      for a limited time. The offer is at a fixed price, usually at a premium over the current market
                      price, and is customarily contingent on shareholders tendering a fixed number of their shares
                      or units.


          LESSON 11.1: COMMENCEMENT OF A TENDER OFFER
                      LO 11.a	Identify the precommencement communications and the tender offer
                                statement.

                      As just mentioned in the introduction to this unit, a tender offer is a means where an investor
                      attempts to gain control of a large portion of a company’s stock by going directly to the
                      shareholders. In a tender offer, the buyer will make an announcement (usually in the form
                      of a newspaper advertisement) of the buyer’s intention to buy a certain number of shares at
                      a stated price, during a specified time. To entice more shareholders to tender their shares,
                      the bidder will usually offer a price higher than the current market price of the stock. Tender

                                                                                                                        185



S79_LEM_5E.indb 185                                                                                                 9/1/2020 1:55:42 PM
          186         Unit 11   Tender Offers and Issuer Repurchases



                                        offers must always be made in good faith. If a bidder conducts a successful tender offer, the
                                        bidder must make the agreed payment and take receipt of the securities.

                                                    TAKE NOTE
                                                    Tender offers can be either cash only or may include a combination of cash and
                                                    securities.


                                        Commencement of a Tender Offer
                                        A tender offer is considered to have commenced at 12:01 am the day the bidder first
                                        announces the means by which shareholders may tender their shares. This announcement can
                                        be either written or oral.


                                        Precommencement Communications
                                        Precommencement communications include any communications about the tender offer
                                        made before the bidder announcing the method to tender the shares. Precommencement
                                        communications must include a prominent, easy-to-read legend advising shareholders to read
                                        the tender offer statement when available and stating that investors can get the tender offer
                                        statement and other documents for free from the SEC’s website or the offerer.

                                                    TEST TOPIC ALERT
                                                    All written precommencement communications must be disclosed on Schedule TO no
                                                    later than the commencement date.


                                        Tender Offer Statement
                                        If a bidder intends to gain control of 5% or more of the subject company’s securities, the
                                        bidder must file a tender offer statement on Schedule TO. Schedule TO must be sent to
                                         the SEC,
                                         FINRA,
                                         the subject company’s principal executive office,
                                         any national securities exchange where the subject company’s shares trade, and
                                         any other bidder who has filed a Schedule TO and has not completed a tender offer.
                                        The bidder must make postcommencement amendments to Schedule TO if there are any
                                        material changes to the information contained in the schedule. A final amendment must also
                                        be made containing the final results of the tender offer when the offering has expired.


                                        Tender Offers Regulations

                                        LO 11.b	Apply the regulations that impact tender offers.



                                        Dissemination of the Tender Offer to Shareholders
                                        Upon receipt of the tender offer statement, the subject company must notify the transfer
                                        agent of the tender offer and prepare a stockholder list. The subject company must then



S79_LEM_5E.indb 186                                                                                                                     9/1/2020 1:55:43 PM
                                                                       Unit 11   Tender Offers and Issuer Repurchases   187


                      supply the bidder with the approximate number of shareholders for the class of securities
                      subject to the tender offer.

                      Once the stockholder list has been compiled, the subject company may either mail tender
                      offer materials directly to the shareholders, or it may provide the bidder with the stockholder
                                                                                                                                  Unit 11
                      list. If the subject company chooses to disclose the stockholder list, any changes to it must be
                      promptly forwarded to the bidder.


                      Equal Treatment of Security Holders
                      Tender offers must be available to all shareholders of the class of security subject to the tender
                      offer. An exception to this rule, however, is a bidder may exclude shareholders who reside in a
                      state where the bidder is prohibited from making the tender offer.


                      Length of Tender Offer
                      To prevent fraudulent or manipulative activity, the SEC has ruled that no tender offer may
                      be open for less than 20 days from commencement. If the securities tendered, however, are
                      registered under Form S-4 or are part of a roll-up transaction, the tender must be open for at
                      least 60 days.

                      When a tender offer is amended to change the percentage of securities being sought by more
                      than 2%, the tender offer must be open for at least an additional 10 business days.

                      The length of a tender offer may not be extended without a press release or other public
                      announcement. The notice must include the approximate number of shares already tendered.
                      The notice must be issued no later than the earlier of
                       9:00 am ET the next business day after the scheduled expiration of the offer or
                       the first opening of any national securities exchange on which the securities are listed on
                         the next business day after the scheduled expiration.


                      Prohibiting Purchases Outside of a Tender Offer
                      Once a tender offer has been made, neither the bidder nor the bidder’s associates and advisors
                      may make any purchase of the subject security outside of the tender offer. Exemptions to this
                      rule include
                       exercises in related securities purchased before the tender offer;
                       covering preexisting obligations;
                       purchases of odd lots (under 100 shares);
                       basket transactions, including over 20 securities purchased in the usual course of business;
                         and
                       purchases made by an independent agent of the issuer.


                      Subject Company’s Position to a Tender Offer
                      Within 10 days of the date a tender offer is first published, the subject company is required
                      to send a statement indicating the company’s position on the tender offer. Its position may
                      be recommending shareholders to accept or reject the tender offer, expressing no opinion, or
                      stating it is unable to take a position, including the reason why it cannot take a position.




S79_LEM_5E.indb 187                                                                                                     9/1/2020 1:55:43 PM
          188         Unit 11   Tender Offers and Issuer Repurchases



                                        Partial Tender Offers
                                        When tendering shares, a shareholder must hold a net long position of at least as many
                                        shares as tendered. A net long position is the shareholder’s long position less the shareholder’s
                                        short position (if any). A long position includes any shares owned and equivalent securities
                                        where the shares are immediately accessible (e.g., an exercisable call option). A short position
                                        includes borrowed shares, unsettled sold shares, or shares covering a short call position.

                                                    EXAMPLE
                                                    An investor owns 3,000 shares of XYZ, a stock currently undergoing a tender offer. She
                                                    also owns warrants immediately convertible into 1,000 shares, and has written five
                                                    covered call options with an exercise price lower than the tender price. The net long
                                                    position for this investor is 3,000 + 1,000 – 500 = 3,500 shares.


                                        Recommendation or Solicitation by the Subject Company and Others
                                        Once a tender offer has commenced, the subject company, its employees, directors, affiliates,
                                        subsidiaries, or beneficial owners may not make any solicitation or recommendation about the
                                        subject securities without filing a Schedule 14D-9 with the SEC as soon as practicable on the
                                        same date. The schedule must also be sent to the principal office of the bidder as well as any
                                        national exchanges on which the subject security is listed (or FINRA if it trades OTC).

                                        If any material change occurs in the materials presented in the schedule, an amendment must
                                        be prepared and promptly sent to the same parties that received the original schedules.


                                        Tender Offers and Insider Information
                                        Just as with any other securities transaction, the SEC has put rules in place to prevent the
                                        misuse of material nonpublic (insider) information during a tender offer. SEC Rule 14e-3
                                        prohibits any person with insider information concerning a tender offer, or that person’s
                                        agents, from acting on that information. Additionally, those who possess insider information
                                        are prohibited from disclosing it to anyone where it is reasonably foreseeable that the
                                        information would be acted upon.

                                                    EXAMPLE
                                                    The bidder’s secretary has recently seen an unreleased memorandum stating that the
                                                    offering price was going to increase. The secretary immediately calls a friend to inform
                                                    her of the price increase, knowing the friend is looking for a short-term profit. The
                                                    secretary has violated SEC Rule 14e-3 by divulging the material nonpublic information
                                                    to someone the secretary could reasonably believe would act on the information by
                                                    buying the subject securities before an announcement of the price increase.

                                                    KNOWLEDGE CHECK
                                                    1.   A tender offer is considered to have begun
                                                          A. at 12:01 am on the day the bidder announces the offer.
                                                          B. at 12:01 pm on the day the bidder announces the offer.
                                                          C. once approved by the shareholders.
                                                          D. at 12:01 am the next business day after the bidder announces the offer.

                             basket transactions, including over 20 securities purchased in the usual
                                 course of business; and
                             purchases made by an independent agent of the issuer. LO 11.b

                       5. B Within 10 days of the date a tender offer is first published, the subject company is
                            required to send a statement indicating the company’s position on the tender offer.
                            LO 11.b

          LESSON 11.2: REPURCHASES BY THE ISSUER
                                        LO 11.c	Recall the choices issuers have by which tender offer shares may be
                                                 acquired.

                                        Occasionally, issuers may wish to repurchase their shares. Once repurchased, the shares may
                                        either be retired by the company, or they may be held as treasury stock to be reissued later
                                        (e.g., upon exercise of a warrant).


                                        Tender Offer Repurchase Programs
                                        When repurchasing shares, issuers have several choices by which they may be acquired.
                                        Repurchases may be done through open market purchases (discussed later) or through a fixed
                                        price Dutch auction tender offer.

                                        If the issuer elects to repurchase its shares through a tender offer, it is subject to all the same
                                        rules and filing requirements as a third-party tender offer.


                                        Fixed Price
                                        The simplest method for an issuer to conduct a tender offer is through a fixed price tender. As
                                        the name implies, a fixed price tender offer is where the issuer states a fixed price for which all
                                        tendered shares will be purchased. If the tender offer is undersubscribed, the issuer may either
                                        return the shares or purchase all the shares tendered at the fixed price. If the tender offer is
                                        oversubscribed, the shares tendered will be selected on a pro-rata basis.


                                        Dutch Auctions
                                        An alternative to the traditional fixed price tender offer is to conduct a Dutch auction. A
                                        Dutch auction is set up by the company announcing either the maximum price or a price
                                        range, where it would be willing to purchase the shares. The shareholders may then submit
                                        offers on where they would be willing to sell their shares. At the expiration of the auction,
                                        the price of the tender offer would be the highest price where the tender would be filled, and
                                        shares are tendered on a pro-rata basis.

                                                    EXAMPLE
                                                    An issuer is willing to buy 10,000 shares in a Dutch auction tender offer with a
                                                    maximum price of $10 per share. In response, the following offers were received:

                                                       Bid Price       Number of Shares
                                                          9.50               1,000
                                                          9.60               2,000
                                                          9.70               2,000
                                                          9.80               3,000
                                                          9.90               4,000
                                                          10.00              3,000
                                                    This tender offer would result in a tender price of 9.90 with shares being taken from
                                                    the bids of 9.90 and below on a pro-rata basis.




S79_LEM_5E.indb 190                                                                                                                           9/1/2020 1:55:44 PM
                                                                          Unit 11   Tender Offers and Issuer Repurchases    191


                       Going Private Transactions (Warren Buffet)
                       When the number of shareholders of a public company drops below 300, the company may
                       deregister its equity securities and is no longer considered to be publicly held. When that
                       occurs, the company is no longer required to file reports with the SEC, and the regulatory
                                                                                                                                      Unit 11
                       burden lessens significantly. As a result, it may be the objective of an investor, or even the
                       subject company itself, to go private.

                       When an investor wishes to make a tender offer for most or all of a company’s shares, the
                       investor may effectively be taking the company private and must follow the same rules and
                       regulations regarding any other tender offer. If, however, the company itself, or an affiliate,
                       is making a tender offer for its own securities to go private, the company must follow the
                       requirements of SEC Rule 13e-3 in addition to other tender offer regulations.

                       Rule 13e-3 requires that the bidder file a Schedule 13E-3, which includes
                        a discussion of the purposes of the transaction,
                        any alternatives that the company considered and whether the transaction is fair to all
                          shareholders,
                        disclosure of whether and why any of its directors disagreed with the transaction, and
                        whether a majority of directors who are not company employees approved the transaction.

                                  TEST TOPIC ALERT
                                  A Schedule 13E-3 must be filed for an issuer or affiliate, regardless of whether or not
                                  the issuer or affiliate is listed on a national securities exchange.


                       Open Market Issuer Repurchases

                       LO 11.d	Identify the conditions to comply with the SEC Safe Harbor Rule 10b-18.

                       The SEC has attempted to control market manipulation of issuers by identifying how an
                       issuer or affiliate may purchase its own stock in the secondary market. If an issuer meets the
                       prescribed conditions, the SEC assumes that it is not attempting to manipulate the market
                       and is buying for a legitimate purpose [such as to fund an employee stock ownership plan
                       (ESOP) or a company pension]. To be within the safe harbor of SEC Rule 10b-18, the
                       following conditions must be met.
                        Transactions on any given day can only be affected through one market maker or
                          designated market makers (DMMs).
                        Transactions on any given day cannot exceed 25% of the average daily trading volume
                          (ADTV) measured over the prior four calendar weeks. Block purchases do count against
                          the daily purchase limit.
                        Transactions cannot affect the opening or closing of a security. A safe harbor is available
                          if the issuer is not involved in the first transaction of the day or any transaction in the last
                          half hour of trading (3:30–4:00 pm ET).
                        Transactions can be executed at prices no higher than the highest independent bid or the
                          last reported sale price, whichever is higher.




S79_LEM_U11.indd 191                                                                                                        9/1/2020 2:41:39 PM
          192          Unit 11   Tender Offers and Issuer Repurchases



                                                     EXAMPLE
                                                     XYZ Corporation is conducting an issuer repurchase program using the safe harbor
                                                     provisions of Rule 10b-18. The following chart shows the current independent bids
                                                     and offers in the stock.

                                                          Bid Size                Bid        Ask            Ask Size
                                                            100                  10.25       10.26             300
                                                            500                  10.24       10.27             200
                                                            300                  10.22       10.28            1,000
                                                            500                  10.20       10.30             300
                                                           1,000                 10.18       10.35             500
                                                     If the last sale was executed at $10.25, the highest bid that could be placed for the
                                                     issuer is $10.25.
                                                     If the last sale was $10.27, the 300 shares offered at $10.26 and 200 shares offered
                                                     at $10.27 could be purchased by the issuer and remain within the provisions of
                                                     Rule 10b-18 because the last sale is higher than the highest independent bid.

                                                     TAKE NOTE
                                                     If an issuer’s security is an actively traded security as defined in Regulation M, the safe
                                                     harbor will not apply for the 10-minute period before market close. For other issuers,
                                                     the safe harbor will not be available for purchases effected within 30 minutes of closing.

                                                     1.   The contents of the merger proxy are governed in accordance with which of the

                                                            A. Schedule 14A
                                                            B. Form 10K
                                                            C. Schedule 14D

                                                     3.   LMN, an affiliate of ABC, a publicly traded company listed on the NYSE, is being
                                                          utilized as the conduit for a tender offer for all outstanding shares of ABC. To be in
                                                          compliance with SEC rules, which of the following is true?
                                                             I. The company must follow the requirements of SEC Rule 13e-3.
                                                            II. The company must submit a discussion of the purposes of the transaction.
                                                           III. The company must disclose any alternatives that the company considered and
                                                                 whether the transaction is fair to all shareholders.
                                                           IV. The company must disclose whether any of its directors disagreed with the
                                                                 transaction.
                                                            A.   I and II
                                                            B.   II and III
                                                            C.   I, II, and III
                                                            D.   I, II, III, and IV




S79_LEM_U11.indd 192                                                                                                                               23/05/22 1:51 PM
                                                               Unit 11   Tender Offers and Issuer Repurchases   193


                      4.   To be within the safe harbor of SEC Rule 10b-18, all the following conditions must be
                           met except
                            A. transactions on any given day can only be affected through one market maker
                                or designated market maker (DMM).

                                                                                                                          Unit 11
                            B. transactions on any given day cannot exceed 25% of the average daily trading
                                volume (ADTV) measured over the prior four calendar weeks. Block purchases
                                do not count against the daily purchase limit.
                            C. A safe harbor is available if the issuer is not involved in the first transaction of
                                the day or any transaction in the last half hour of trading (3:30–4:00 pm ET).
                            D. Transactions can be executed at prices no higher than the highest
                                independent bid or the last reported sale price, whichever is higher.

                      Answers
                      1. A For public companies, the SEC requires that a proxy statement includes specific
                           information as set forth in Schedule 14A. These information requirements, as
                           relevant in M&A transactions, generally include a summary term sheet, background
                           of the transaction, recommendation of the board(s), fairness opinion(s), summary
                           financial and pro forma data, and the definitive agreement, among many other
                           items either required or deemed pertinent for shareholders to make an informed
                           decision on the transaction. Schedule 14D-9 is a recommendation from the target’s
                           board of directors on how shareholders should respond to a tender offer. LO 11.c

                      2. A The simplest method for an issuer to conduct a tender offer is through a fixed price
                           tender. As the name implies, a fixed price tender offer is where the issuer states a
                           fixed price for which all tendered shares will be purchased. LO 11.c

                      3. D Rule 13e-3 requires that the bidder file a Schedule 13E-3, which includes
                            a discussion of the purposes of the transaction,
                            any alternatives that the company considered and whether the transaction

                            disclosure of whether and why any of its directors disagreed with the
                                transaction, and
                            whether a majority of directors who are not company employees approved
                                the transaction. LO 11.c
                      4. B The exception here is that block purchases do count against the daily purchase
                           limit. The others are correct. LO 11.d

           UNIT


     12                                  Distressed Companies




          LEARNING OBJECTIVES
                      When you have completed this unit, you will be able to accomplish the following.
                      ff LO 12.a	Recall the terms of a loan document.
                      ff LO 12.b	Select the appropriate type of bankruptcy filing.
                      ff LO 12.c	Recognize when to apply Section 363 of the Bankruptcy Code.



          INTRODUCTION
                      Not all companies that an investment bank deals with will be in good financial standing.
                      Occasionally, there will be an investment opportunity with a distressed company—one that
                      is either close to or has already entered bankruptcy. Before engaging in any transaction with a
                      distressed company, it is vital to understand why the company is distressed and what type of
                      bankruptcy, if any, has been filed.


          LESSON 12.1: DEALING WITH DISTRESSED COMPANIES

                      Terms of Loan Documents

                      LO 12.a	Recall the terms of a loan document.

                      Before entering into any credit arrangement with a company, the creditor will require the
                      company to sign a credit agreement, or indenture. The indenture is the governing document
                      of the loan, detailing all the terms of the loan, including the principal and interest to be paid
                      and any covenants entered. The rights of the creditor and the responsibilities of the borrower
                      are specified in the indenture.

                                                                                                                          195



S79_LEM_5E.indb 195                                                                                                   9/1/2020 1:55:45 PM
          196         Unit 12   Distressed Companies



                                       Repayment
                                       The most straightforward portion of a credit agreement is the provision that the loan will be
                                       repaid. The indenture will specify the date repayment is required (if a date exists) and any
                                       penalties for failure to repay the loan. The indenture will also include the amount of interest
                                       the borrower is required to pay and the frequency of the interest payments (including any
                                       minimum payments required).


                                       Prepayment
                                       A creditor enters into a loan agreement to be compensated through interest payments. In the
                                       event a firm repays its loan early, the interest stream to the creditor would cease. To mitigate
                                       this prepayment risk, an indenture may include provisions that prevent the borrower from
                                       prepaying or subject the borrower to a penalty in the case of prepayment (e.g., the present
                                       value of all unpaid interest payments).


                                       Events of Default
                                       Several events may result in the default of a loan. The most common event specified in
                                       the credit agreement is missing a periodic interest payment. Other events that would be
                                       considered defaulting may include failing to maintain certain financial ratios or the sale of an
                                       asset securing the loan.


                                       Negative Covenants
                                       Negative covenants, also referred to as restrictive covenants, bind an issuer to not engage in
                                       certain activities without the creditor’s consent. Negative covenants are written to help protect
                                       the creditor’s security in payment of both interest and principal. Negative covenants generally
                                       include limitations on dividends that can be paid, limits on new issues of debt, and seniority
                                       of future debt.


                                       Financial Covenants
                                       Financial covenants are a type of affirmative covenant into which the borrower enters. They
                                       require the borrower to continue to meet financial standards laid out in the indenture. These
                                       standards are set to ensure the borrower can meet its required payments and, thus, generally
                                       deal with the liquidity of the borrower.

                                                   TAKE NOTE
                                                   If the borrower fails to meet its financial covenants, the loan is considered in default.


                                       Bankruptcy
                                       LO 12.b	Select the appropriate type of bankruptcy filing.

                                       When a company becomes insolvent, it is given the opportunity under Title 11 of the U.S.
                                       Code to file for bankruptcy. Title 11, otherwise known as the Bankruptcy Code, offers several
                                       ways to declare bankruptcy. Most companies declare one of two types (classified by their
                                       chapter in the Bankruptcy Code): Chapter 7 (liquidation) or Chapter 11 (reorganization).




S79_LEM_5E.indb 196                                                                                                                            9/1/2020 1:55:46 PM
                                                                                        Unit 12   Distressed Companies    197


                       Chapter 7 (Liquidation)
                       When a company reaches a point where it can no longer pay its creditors, an option it has
                       is to file for bankruptcy under Chapter 7 of the Bankruptcy Code. When a firm files for
                       Chapter 7 bankruptcy, all business activities must cease, and the court will appoint a trustee
                       to oversee the liquidation of all the company’s assets, in an attempt to meet its obligations.
                       This ultimately results in the dissolution of the company.

                       While Chapter 7 allows individuals to have a fresh start, no such provision is given to
                       partnerships or corporations. The company is dissolved and no longer exists, but any unpaid
                       debts still remain, albeit only until the statute of limitations on the debts expires. As a result, a
                       Chapter 7 filing is the final (and least common) option for a company in trouble.


                       Priority of Investors During Bankruptcy
                       When a firm is liquidated in connection with a Chapter 7 bankruptcy, not all investors are
                       treated equally. Different classes of securities have different levels of priority. The priority for       Unit 12
                       each class of security is (from most senior to junior)
                        senior secured creditors (senior debt lenders),
                        junior secured creditors (senior subordinated debt),
                        unsecured creditors (trade suppliers),
                        mezzanine (convertible debt),
                        preferred stock, and
                        common stock.

                                  TEST TOPIC ALERT
                                  During a liquidation, unpaid wages, back taxes, and general creditors are paid before
                                  any security holder.
                       It is unlikely common shareholders will recoup their investments, because they have the
                       lowest seniority during a liquidation. This risk is one of the reasons that the required rate of
                       return on common stock is generally higher than for any other security.


                       Chapter 11 (Reorganization)
                       While a Chapter 7 bankruptcy represents the classical view of a bankruptcy, where the
                       company is completely liquidated and ceases to exist, a Chapter 11 bankruptcy allows
                       significantly more leeway through a reorganization of the company’s debt.
                       Unlike Chapter 7, Chapter 11 bankruptcy allows the company to continue to operate
                       and be run by the management of the company (debtor in possession). Once the filing is
                       made, an automatic stay is put on all claims against the debtor. While the stay prevents any
                       further action to be taken against the debtor until the matter can be resolved either through
                       bankruptcy court or once the debtor emerges from bankruptcy, it does not absolve the debtor
                       of its obligation.

                                  TEST TOPIC ALERT
                                  While the debtor in possession (DIP) remains in control of the company and its assets,
                                  the DIP may not sell or transfer any assets that are securing a loan or investment.




S79_LEM_U12.indd 197                                                                                                     9/3/2020 1:25:39 PM
          198          Unit 12   Distressed Companies



                                        Reorganization Plan
                                        The ultimate goal of a Chapter 11 bankruptcy is the implementation of a plan of
                                        reorganization that will allow the company to survive (albeit in a different form) and to pay all
                                        its creditors. The reorganization plan separates creditors into separate classes such as secured
                                        creditors, unsecured creditors entitled to priority, general unsecured creditors, and equity
                                        security holders. Because all creditors may not be completely paid, those whose claims will not
                                        be paid completely are considered impaired.

                                        The plan may only be proposed by the company in the first 120 days of the Chapter 11
                                        filing. After this time, barring an extension granted by the court, the credit committee, a U.S.
                                        trustee, or another interested party may also propose a reorganization plan.

                                        In order for the plan to be accepted, it must be approved by the noninsider creditors. An
                                        entire class of creditors is deemed to have accepted the plan if the creditors holding two-thirds
                                        of the principal of the class’s claims and at least half of the claimants accept the plan. If there
                                        is dissention between the creditors in accepting the plan, it can still be accepted by the court
                                        if the first class of noninsider, impaired creditors accepts the plan. This is referred to as a cram
                                        down because the dissenting creditors are forced to accept the plan.

                                                    TAKE NOTE
                                                    A reorganization plan may involve the liquidation of the company. This may be
                                                    preferable to a Chapter 7 bankruptcy filing because the DIP may be able to glean
                                                    greater value from the liquidation than a trustee.


                                        U.S. Trustee
                                        When the company makes a Chapter 11 filing, the court appoints a U.S. trustee to oversee
                                        the progress and administration of the company while in bankruptcy. The debtor is required
                                        to meet with the U.S. trustee in a Section 341 meeting to ensure the debtor has made the
                                        appropriate applications and made financial statements (including tax returns) available.
                                        Should the debtor fail to meet its obligations to the court or the trustee, the trustee may
                                        make a motion to the bankruptcy court to convert the debtor’s case to another chapter of the
                                        Bankruptcy Code (e.g., Chapter 7).


                                        Creditor Committee
                                        To aid in ensuring accountability to creditors, the U.S. trustee appoints a creditor committee,
                                        generally consisting of the largest seven unsecured creditors. While the creditor committee
                                        does not operate the business, it does consult with the DIP, investigates the debtor’s conduct
                                        in business operations, and assists in formulating a plan to exit Chapter 11.

                                                    TAKE NOTE
                                                    While the creditor committee is generally made up of the largest seven unsecured
                                                    creditors, the U.S. Trustee may create other committees made up of secured creditors
                                                    or shareholders.


                                        Debtor-in-Possession (DIP) Financing
                                        After a firm has made a Chapter 11 filing, it may still need to raise additional capital to
                                        continue its operations. The new capital raised is DIP financing. Because the company is
                                        already in bankruptcy, however, it may have difficulty raising DIP financing. As a result, the




S79_LEM_U12.indd 198                                                                                                                       9/3/2020 1:25:40 PM
                                                                                        Unit 12   Distressed Companies   199


                       court may allow these creditors to gain higher seniority than other creditors as an enticement
                       to invest in the struggling company.

                                 TEST TOPIC ALERT
                                 If a company is listed on a stock exchange, it is usually delisted once it enters
                                 bankruptcy and trades subsequently on the OTC Markets. When trading on these
                                 markets, it has the letter Q appended to the end of its symbol to indicate the company
                                 is in bankruptcy.

                                 KNOWLEDGE CHECK
                                 1.   All of the following statements are true except
                                       A. prior to entering into any credit agreement, the creditor will require the
                                             company to enter into an indenture.
                                       B. the indenture is the governing document of the loan.

                                                                                                                                  Unit 12
                                       C. the rights of the creditor and the responsibilities of the borrower are specified
                                             in the indenture.
                                       D. The rights of the borrower and the responsibilities of the creditor are specified
                                             in the indenture.
                                 2.   The most common event specified in the credit agreement that may result in the

                                 3.   A credit agreement indenture includes a restriction on the borrower’s ability to use

                                       A. last right asset.

                                       C. negative covenant.
                                       D. prohibitive use restriction.
                                 4.   Title 11 of the U.S. Code is otherwise known as

                                 1. D Before entering into any credit arrangement with a company, the creditor will
                                      require the company to enter into a credit agreement, or indenture. The indenture
                                      is the governing document of the loan, detailing all the terms of the loan, including

                                      creditor and the responsibilities of the borrower are specified in the indenture.
                                      LO 12.a

          200         Unit 12   Distressed Companies



                                                   2. A Missing a periodic interest payment will be a reason to call the loan in default.
                                                        Exceeding financial ratios is most often a good thing and the sale of an asset
                                                        securing the loan would be a concern, while purchasing an asset would be viewed
                                                        as growing the business as long as it was in line and would certainly not be seen as
                                                        a default. LO 12.a

                                                   3. C Restrictive covenants, also called negative covenants, protect creditors by
                                                        restricting the borrower’s ability to use corporate capital or assets in ways that
                                                        could undermine the lender’s ability to be repaid principal and interest. Examples
                                                        of this would include prohibitions against payment of a special dividend or
                                                        pledging key assets as collateral. LO 12.a

                                                        the U.S. Code to file for bankruptcy. Title 11 is otherwise known as the Bankruptcy
                                                        Code. LO 12.b

                                                        continue operating as a “going concern” while it attempts to restructure its financial
                                                        obligations. During bankruptcy, while secured creditors are generally stayed from
                                                        enforcing their remedies, they are entitled to certain protections and rights not
                                                        provided to unsecured creditors (including the right to continue to receive interest
                                                        payments). LO 12.b


          LESSON 12.2: MERGERS AND ACQUISITIONS DURING BANKRUPTCY
                                       LO 12.c	Recognize when to apply Section 363 of the Bankruptcy Code.

                                       The traditional method of selling a distressed company is through the acceptance of a bid by
                                       the creditors and stockholders. However, this process is very time consuming (taking up to
                                       multiple years to complete) and costly. Section 363 of the Bankruptcy Code, on the other
                                       hand, allows for quick sales of a company’s assets. These sales, known as Section 363 sales,
                                       permit much faster timelines and fewer hurdles to overcome. Due to these advantages, there
                                       is a greater tendency for Section 363 sales to occur than the traditional sale of a distressed
                                       company.


                                       Bidding Process
                                       A 363 sale is very similar to a traditional auction, where multiple parties may bid for the
                                       ownership of the company’s assets. Once the assets are put on auction, bids may be received,
                                       and the highest bid wins the assets, with court approval. The final settlement of the auction
                                       generally occurs within four to six weeks of the auction’s close, thus, greatly speeding along
                                       the process of the sale from years to months.


                                       Stalking Horse
                                       Participants in a 363 sale must be aware, however, of frequently used provisions for the initial
                                       bidder, also known as a stalking horse. Once a determination to sell the company’s assets has
                                       been made, the DIP will frequently seek out a stalking horse, who will set the base price for
                                       the sale, and only attract more favorable bids.




S79_LEM_5E.indb 200                                                                                                                        9/1/2020 1:55:48 PM
                                                                                       Unit 12   Distressed Companies     201


                      In return for being the first bid and the time and expense invested in a potentially losing
                      position, the stalking horse is generally compensated through
                       a breakup fee if the bid is not accepted,
                       reimbursement of due diligence expenses,
                       restrictions on third-party bidders,
                       minimum increments for additional bids, and
                       short deadlines for additional bids.
                      While the stalking horse does provide the advantage that there is an initial bid, with a base
                      price for the sale, it does come with disadvantages to the distressed company as well. Because
                      there are generally restrictions on other buyers, most notably the shortened response time and
                      minimum bid increments, the stalking horse may cause some potential bidders to refrain from
                      engaging in the bidding process.

                                KNOWLEDGE CHECK                                                                                    Unit 12
                                1.   In a Section 363 000000transaction, the major creditor involved in the takeover is

             Volume-Weighted Average Price (VWAP) The VWAP                      zero-coupon bond A corporate or municipal debt
             is the price at which most trading in a stock took place in a      security traded at a deep discount from face value.
             given period. It is determined by multiplying the price by         The bond pays no interest; rather, it may be redeemed
